OVERVIEW: Evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of second degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. 802 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Fru-Con Constr. Corp. v. Xchanging


11-529


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


11-529 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/14/11); 81 So. 3d 209; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1571



December 14, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ dismissed by Fru-Con Constr. Corp. v. Xchanging, 84 So. 3d 561, 2012 La. LEXIS 741 (La., Mar. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 02, LASALLE PARISH, NO. 10-10742. JAMES BRADDOCK, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Employer's claim for declaratory relief given a conflict between the recommendations of an employee's treating physician and an independent medical examiner was dismissed because the employer failed to comply with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1314. The employer's remedy, if it believed the IME was correct, was to terminate benefits at its peril. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(G), the court could not address the constitutionality of § 23:1314 because the employer failed to raise it in the workers' compensation court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the employer's claim.

804 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


No. 46,742-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,742 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/14/11); 79 So. 3d 1278; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1555



December 14, 2011, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 156,113. Honorable Michael O. Craig, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The denial of defendant's motion to suppress the evidence was proper because there was no merit in his argument that the traffic stop was unlawful in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV. Under the facts, probable cause for a traffic violation under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:71(B) existed, and the driver was ultimately ticketed for that violation. The caution barriers on the shoulder did not prevent the normal traffic flow in the right-hand lane of the interstate highway. The officers also had a basis for reasonable suspicion of additional criminal activity and for extending the stop.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Fru-Con Constr. Corp. v. Moore


11-528


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


11-528 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/14/11); 81 So. 3d 202; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1566



December 14, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ dismissed by Fru-Con Constr. Corp. v. Moore, 84 So. 3d 561, 2012 La. LEXIS 733 (La., Mar. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION DISTRICT 2, GRANT PARISH, NO. 10-10536. JAMES BRADDOCK, WORKERS COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: An employer filed a petition for declaratory judgment, asking the workers' compensation judge (WCJ) to decide what course of treatment an employee had to follow. It challenged the WCJ's decision to grant the employee's exception of no cause of action. The employer failed to meet the requirements of the Louisiana Worker's Compensation Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1314. It could not bring an action that did not comply with the provisions of § 23:1314 because the WCJ was duty bound to dismiss the action as premature and was prohibited from addressing any other issue in the proceeding.


OUTCOME: Decision affirmed in part and remanded.

Street v. Bridges


No. 46,765-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,765 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/14/11); 80 So. 3d 1153; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1554



December 14, 2011, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 2010-4192. Honorable Hamilton Stephens Winters, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment that upheld an assessment of penalties by appellee state department of revenue under La. R.S. 47:1602(A) for his failure to timely pay his taxes. The appellate court found, inter alia, that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5104 required that the taxpayer's protest be filed in the district court of the judicial district in which the state capitol was located. In addition, the taxpayer failed to following the payment protest procedures in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:15(15). Therefore, the trial court properly dismissed his suit.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed and remanded with instructions.

State v. Rubens


NO. 2010-KA-1114


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-1114 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/30/11); 83 So. 3d 30; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1447



November 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by State v. Rubens, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 180 (La.App. 4 Cir., Jan. 11, 2012)
Writ denied by State v. Rubens, 90 So. 3d 410, 2012 La. LEXIS 1567 (La., May 25, 2012)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Rubens v. State, 99 So. 3d 37, 2012 La. LEXIS 2886 (La., Oct. 12, 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Rubens v. Cain, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 186017 (E.D. La., Sept. 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 481-108, SECTION "F". Honorable Robin D. Pittman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In defendant's trial on a charge of second-degree murder for the killing of a man with whom defendant's girfriend was having an affair, the trial court did not err under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 404(B)(1) in admitting into evidence angry and threatening voicemail messages left by defendant the day before the killing regarding the conversations he had with the victim because such evidence was relevant and admissible as proof of motive. Evidence of the angry telephone calls tended to show that defendant bore a grudge toward the victim and did not act in self-defense in killing him.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of second-degree murder and sentencing defendant to life imprisonment at hard labor was affirmed.

 

810 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re Succession of Bailey


NO. 11-CA-147


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


11-147 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/29/11); 82 So. 3d 322; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1427



November 29, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 1, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 672-095, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The time period for appellants to establish filiation had prescribed. Because repealed La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209 was the clear and unambiguous positive law in effect at the time appellants reached the age of nineteen, equitable estoppel could not prevail against art. 209, which mandated appellants to establish filiation within one year of the death of their alleged father or within nineteen years of their births, whichever occurred first. Accordingly, the application of equitable estoppel was not justified.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Lomax


NO. 2011-KA-0591


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2011-0591 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/28/11); 81 So. 3d 788; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1419



November 28, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 471-564, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Q. Alarcon, Judge.
State v. Lomax, 51 So. 3d 2, 2010 La. LEXIS 2668 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: HABITUAL OFFENDER CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant's life sentence as a triple offender for heroin possession under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(C)(1) was affirmed. The State met its La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1D(1)(b) burden. Defendant had been convicted of the predicate offenses under guilty pleas and knowingly and voluntarily had waived his constitutional rights. An officer testified that the fingerprints taken for defendant's simple robbery conviction matched the fingerprints in this case. A transcript was presented of a prior heroin possession case, in which defendant admitted that he had pled guilty to first-degree robbery.

Martinez v. Tanner


2011 CA 0692


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2011 0692 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/09/11); 79 So. 3d 1082; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1337



November 9, 2011, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Martinez v. Tanner, 2012 La. LEXIS 2028 (La., July 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 581, 100, Section 24. The Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The application of the amended good time forfeiture provisions to an inmate did not violate the ex post facto provisions of the Louisiana and United States Constitutions because the definition of the criminal conduct committed by the inmate was not changed by the amendment to the good time forfeiture statute that occurred after he committed the crimes for which he was convicted and sentenced. Nor did the application of the amended versions of the good time forfeiture law increase the penalty by which the inmate's crime was punishable.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Harris


NO. 2011 KA 0779


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2011 0779 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/09/11); 79 So. 3d 1037; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1348



November 9, 2011, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 495633. Honorable William J. Burris, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Detective had probable cause to search the passenger compartment of a vehicle pursuant to the automobile exception, with or without consent, where the detective's approach of the vehicle was proper, defendant exhibited nervous behavior at the time of the encounter, and the distinct odor of burnt marijuana emanated from him as he exited the vehicle. Although defendant was handcuffed and positioned at the rear of the vehicle, the detective was outnumbered and a weapon was observed in the vehicle. Also, defendant failed to prove that he had a valid prescription for the dextroamphetamine seized.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

815 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lara


No. 46,639-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,639 (La. 11/02/11) 78 So. 3d 159; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1289



November 2, 2011, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 10F0482. Honorable C. Wendell Manning, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court erred in ordering defendant to serve an additional two years' time in prison in default of payment of a fine. The additional two years' imprisonment for default of payment of the fine was a violation of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 884, which limited additional time imposed to one year. The imposition of any jail time for defendant was error because he was indigent. Defendant was represented at trial and on appeal by the indigent defender's office. An indigent person could not be incarcerated because he or she was unable to pay a fine that was part of his or her sentence.


OUTCOME: Sentence imposing jail time in default of payment of fine vacated.

 

816 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Smitko v. Gulf South Shrimp, Inc.


2010 CA 0531


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 0531 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/19/11); 77 So. 3d 1012; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1228



October 19, 2011, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Smitko v. Gulf South Shrimp, Inc., 82 So. 3d 273, 2012 La. LEXIS 474 (La., 2012)
Reversed by, Remanded by Smitko v. Gulf South Shrimp, Inc., 2012 La. LEXIS 1963 (La., July 2, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NUMBER 149,864, PARISH OF TERREBONNE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE JOHN R. WALKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In a quiet title action by a tax purchaser, the former property owner did not institute a timely proceeding to annul, pursuant to former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2228 (now La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2266) and La. Const. art. 7, § 25. Accordingly, the former owner failed to rebut the presumption of regularity afforded to the tax deed. Thus, the burden of proof never shifted to the purchaser's successor to prove that all requisites for a valid tax sale were complied with. Therefore, the successor was entitled to summary judgment because there were no genuine issues of material fact.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Mulder


NO. 2011-KA-0424


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2011-0424 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/19/11); 76 So. 3d 1241; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1234



October 19, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 12, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Mulder, 76 So. 3d 1160, 2011 La. LEXIS 3037 (La., Dec. 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 499-143, SECTION "I". Honorable Karen K. Herman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CONVICTION AND SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The denial of defendant's suppression motion was reversed. The officers did not have a reasonable suspicion under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. art. 215.1(A) that defendant was committing an offense as the mere fact that defendant was walking through the housing development did not constitute trespassing. The officer could not articulate a single factor indicating that she had any safety concerns, much less an objectively reasonable one. The pat down search was a de facto arrest without probable cause in violation of the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, and art. 251.1(B).


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Conviction and sentence vacated. Matter remanded.

State v. Bivens


11-156


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


11-156 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/05/11); 74 So. 3d 782; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1146



October 5, 2011, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF GRANT, NO. 10-253. HONORABLE WARREN DANIEL WILLETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Sufficient evidence supported a conviction for possession with intent to distribute cocaine under La. Rev. Stat. McCann v. McCann


2010 CW 1896 R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 1896 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/05/11); 77 So. 3d 997; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1155



October 5, 2011, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by McCann v. McCann, 78 So. 3d 130, 2012 La. LEXIS 183 (La., 2012)
Reversed by McCann v. McCann, 2012 La. LEXIS 1320 (La., May 8, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Application for Supervisory Review from The Family Court In and For East Baton Rouge Parish. Docket No. 169,863. Honorable Pamela J. Baker, Judge Presiding.
McCann v. Blackwell, 60 So. 3d 1240, 2011 La. LEXIS 842 (La., 2011)



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The issues related to a community property partition action under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2374(C) were within the exclusive subject matter jurisdiction of the family court, and the husband's executrix was the proper person to be substituted into the suit after his death, pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 428, 734, 801, and 802. While the action for divorce, alone, would have been a personal action, the action to divide the former community property and allocate debts was heritable, and thus not a personal action, pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 1765 and 1766.


OUTCOME: Supervisory writ denied.

State v. Hardy


11-267


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


11-267 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/05/11); 72 So. 3d 1017; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1172



October 5, 2011, Decided

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support her conviction for second degree murder in that she had no choice but to shoot the victim. The court concluded that defendant did not show a reasonable belief that the use of deadly force was necessary to avoid imminent danger and that the State's evidence negated the self-defense claim beyond a reasonable doubt. At the time of the shooting, the victim was lying on a couch, and, according to testimony, defendant immediately began shooting as she walked into the apartment without a word or gesture from the victim.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

822 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


11-160


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


11-160 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/05/11); 74 So. 3d 284; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1142



October 5, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Sanders, 85 So. 3d 115, 2012 La. LEXIS 859 (La., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sanders v. Louisiana, 133 S. Ct. 222, 184 L. Ed. 2d 114, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6852 (U.S., 2012)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Sanders v. State, 152 So. 3d 147, 2014 La. LEXIS 2464 (La., 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Sanders v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 174599 (W.D. La., Oct. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 295323. HONORABLE JOHN C. DAVIDSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of second degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The jury heard from several eyewitnesses to the events who identified defendant as the perpetrator. The record presented no basis for re-evaluation of the jury's decision to credit the testimony of the State's witnesses. When the evidence was viewed in the light most favorable to the prosecution, it supported the view that defendant killed the victim by deliberately placing the barrel of a gun within a few inches of his head and firing.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The general damages cap, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B), a part of the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq., unconstitutionally discriminated against a child and her parents, victims of nurse practitioners' malpractice, because of the severity of the child's condition when compared to other malpractice victims who received full recovery. No. 468,417, a matter that had previously been consolidated with Dkt. Nos. 480,159; 480,160; 480,161; 480,162; 480,163; 480,373; 489,776; 489,777; 489,778; 489,779; 489,780; 489,803; 491,530; 491,744; 491,745; 491,746; 491,912; 503,466; 503,468; 503,469; 503,470; 515,414; 515,415; and 515,416. CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In a case concerning a challenge of the ad valorem taxes assessed against a company's public service pipelines, parish assessors had no right of action under La. Rev. Stat. The assessors' cross-appeals were really interventions, and there was clearly no prejudice by the improper labeling of the assessors' pleadings.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. Motion for leave to submit additional documents with brief denied.

State v. Landfair


NO. 2010-KA-1693


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-1693 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/20/11); 70 So. 3d 1061; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 892



July 20, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 22, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 475-405, SECTION "B". Honorable Lynda Van Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant said it was error to sentence him as a fourth felony offender, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(B), because his prior predicate convictions did not follow a chronological sequence of first offense and conviction, followed by second offense and conviction, and so forth. The appellate court held that, while it had been the rule that prior predicate convictions follow such a chronological sequence, there was no error because the statute was amended to remove such a sequential requirement, so his latest conviction only had to follow his prior conviction or convictions, which it did.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Morgan v. City of Shreveport


No. 46,362-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,362 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/13/11); 71 So. 3d 1104; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 871



July 13, 2011, Judgment Rendered

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 516,307. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Firefighters challenged an order granting a city summary judgment and dismissing their action alleging that the city had no authority to enact an incentive pay plan. The city had the authority to set up an incentive pay plan. Its power to set up the plan was not expressly denied by statute or constitution. La. Const. art. VI, § 5 granted broad powers of home rule, and the city's home rule charter accepted that broad power. The incentive pay the firefighters received was part of their salary. The plan of the civil service board was concurrent or supplemental to any pay plan the city set up.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2005-5453, DIVISION "B-15". Honorable Rosemary Ledet, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: New Orleans, La., Mun. Code § 22035 became effective on August 8, 2005 and was to be applied prospectively only. The installation and implementation of park-and-display stations in January 2005 changed the parking meter system throughout the city. Citizens were entitled to notice that the stations were being used to issue citations for violations, in lieu of coin-operated meters. That was especially important for those areas in which both the meters and the stations were simultaneously operational. Because the ordinance was civil, it did not offend the prohibition against ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: Summary judgments affirmed and matter remanded.

State ex rel. AC v. MD


NUMBER 2010 CA 1799


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010-1799 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/17/11); 70 So. 3d 159; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 785



June 17, 2011, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from Twenty-First Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, State of Louisiana. Docket Number 2007-3104. Honorable Zorraine M. Waguespack, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The father acknowledged paternity of a child in 2005; however, he was later shown not to be the biological father of the child. At the time he executed the acknowledgment, he acquired the right to revoke the acknowledgment pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:392(A)(7)(b); there was no time limitation under the prior statute. In 2008, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:406 was amended to limit the time for filing an action to revoke an acknowledgment of paternity. The court held that because this time limit divested the father of a vested right, § 9:406 could only apply prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the father's petition.

State v. Ourso


10-1133


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


10-1133 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/01/11); 67 So. 3d 684; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 711



June 1, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Ourso, 67 So. 3d 680, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 710 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 6902 07. HONORABLE DAVID A. RITCHIE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE FOR POSSESSION OF COCAINE WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE AFFIRMED. SENTENCE FOR POSSESSION OF METHYLENEDIOXYMETHAMPHETAMINE (MDMA) WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING. MOTION TO WITHDRAW DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and possession of methylenedioxymethamphetamine (MDMA) with intent to distribute. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, sentenced him 20 years on each count to run concurrently. Defendant appealed, challenging his sentences. His counsel sought to withdraw pursuant to Anders.


OVERVIEW: In conducting an error patent review pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 920, the court found that defendant's sentence for possession of MDMA with intent to distribute was incorrect. At the time of his offense, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(1) provided that such a conviction required a term of imprisonment between 5 and 30 years with at least 5 years served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. However, the trial court's sentence did not specify how many years were to be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. As the statute gave the trial court discretion as to the number of years imposed to be served without benefits, the court had to vacate the sentence and remand for resentencing. Because the court vacated the sentence, further proceedings remained, and counsel's motion to withdraw was denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and his sentence for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. The court vacated defendant's sentence for possession of MDMA with intent to distribute and remanded for resentencing. The court denied counsel's motion to withdraw.

860 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hoskins


NO. 10-KA-650


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


10-650 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/24/11); 66 So. 3d 1186; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 650



May 24, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 1, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-5359, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Hoskins, 40 So. 3d 199, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 576 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to theft of loud speakers valued at over $ 1,000 in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67B. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, deferred his sentence and placed him on 2 years of probation. His probation was subsequently revoked, and the trial court sentenced defendant to 10 years at hard labor. Defendant sought review, challenging his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a teenager at the time of the crime, contended that the imposition of the maximum sentence under § 14:67B was clearly excessive. Defendant's probation was revoked because he tested positive for marijuana and he subsequently provided a false urine test. He stipulated to the revocation of probation as the trial court recommended boot camp. Approximately one year after the revocation, defendant filed a motion to reconsider sentence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1 as his medication prevented him from attending boot camp. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant along with two co-defendants stole loud speakers from a school. He had no prior criminal record. The court concluded that the maximum sentence was not warranted as it did not involve the most serious violation of § 14:67B nor the worst type of offender. After it was shown defendant could not attend boot camp, the imposition of the sentence was a purposeless infliction of pain and the trial court abused its discretion. The court found a sentence between 2 to 4 years seemed appropriate under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Jacobs

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-887 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/24/11); 67 So. 3d 535; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 636



May 24, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Jacobs, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 914 (La.App. 5 Cir., July 7, 2011)
Writ denied by State v. Jacobs, 80 So. 3d 468, 2012 La. LEXIS 333 (La., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jacobs v. Louisiana, 133 S. Ct. 139, 184 L. Ed. 2d 67, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6681 (U.S., 2012)
Writ denied by State v. Jacobs, 165 So. 3d 69, 2015 La. LEXIS 662 (La., 2015)
Writ denied by Jacobs v. Cain, 168 So. 3d 394, 2015 La. LEXIS 790 (La., 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON REMAND FROM THE LOUISIANA SUPREME COURT, AN APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-7161, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE KERNAN A. HAND, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Jacobs, 32 So. 3d 227, 2010 La. LEXIS 647 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of one count of first-degree murder for the homicide of two victims under La. Rev. Stat. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State failed to exclude the reasonable hypothesis that he was guilty of manslaughter. Defendant contended that the State's evidence showed that he had terminated his involvement in the burglary and had begun to flee when his co-defendant shot and killed the victims. Defendant argued that his statement indicated he participated in an unarmed burglary and that the State failed to present evidence to establish that his gun was operable. The State contended that the evidence clearly showed that defendant was engaged in the commission of an aggravated burglary and an armed robbery that resulted in two homicides. The decision was upheld because it was immaterial whether defendant's gun was unloaded or inoperable. Defendant admitted that he entered a house with a gun and removed property from the victims. Defendant stated that he told the female victim to go into the living room then loaded the van with items taken from the residence. Thus, the evidence supported a finding that defendant committed both aggravated burglary and armed robbery. Even if he only intended to rob the victims, as he claimed in his statement, this would not absolve him from responsibility.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Collins


NO. 2010-KA-0757


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0757 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/11/11); 65 So. 3d 271; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 576



May 11, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Collins, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 905 (La.App. 4 Cir., June 29, 2011)
Writ denied by State v. Collins, 76 So. 3d 1153, 2011 La. LEXIS 2926 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State v. Collins, 78 So. 3d 140, 2012 La. LEXIS 148 (La., 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Collins v. Cain, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 129793 (E.D. La., Aug. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 479-689, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Taylor, 15 So. 3d 1007, 2009 La. LEXIS 2437 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of second-degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued, inter alia, that the trial court improperly allowed a child witness to testify by closed-circuit television rather than in the court room in violation of the Confrontation Clause of U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court of appeal disagreed. Where necessary to protect a child witness from trauma that would be caused by testifying in the physical presence of the defendant, at least where such trauma would impair the child's ability to communicate, the Confrontation Clause did not prohibit use of a procedure that, despite the absence of face-to-face confrontation, ensured the reliability of the evidence by subjecting it to rigorous adversarial testing and preserved the essence of effective communication. An expert testified for the State that if the child were required to testify in open court, he would likely suffer extreme emotional distress and would have been unable to reasonably communicate to the jury. The expert's testimony conformed to the Maryland v. Craig standard that the emotional distress the child witness would suffer in the presence of the defendants was more than de minimis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hall


NO. 2010-KA-1516


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-1516 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/13/11) 64 So. 3d 339; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 462



April 13, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 17, 2011.
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Hall, 2013 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 147 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 400-281, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.
State v. Hall, 817 So. 2d 514, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1614 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 24, 2002)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of possession of cocaine and sentenced to life in prison as a third felony offender. He sought post-conviction relief, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel as his attorney failed to appeal from a district court's denial of his motion to correct an illegal sentence and motion to reconsider sentence. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied his application. He sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that his sentence was excessive under the amendments to the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1529.1, which no longer mandated a life sentence. At the hearing on the motion to reconsider sentence, the district court found that under § 15:1529.1, appellant was still eligible for a life sentence at the discretion of the sentencing court. The court found that the district court misstated the sentencing range under § 15:1529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii), which provided a maximum sentence of 10 years under the circumstances of the case. It did not appear that the district court felt it had the discretion to impose a sentence other than life. While amendments to § 15:1529.1, which reduced mandatory minimum sentences, had prospective application only, the district court could have and should have considered the amendments in determining whether appellant's mandatory minimum sentence was constitutionally excessive. The court concluded that remand was appropriate to afford appellant the opportunity to prove that the mandatory minimum sentence was unconstitutionally excessive as applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the apparent life sentence and remanded for a new hearing on the motion to reconsider sentence.

State v. Cass


No. 46,228-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,228 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/13/11); 61 So. 3d 840; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 436



April 13, 2011, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Cass, 75 So. 3d 922, 2011 La. LEXIS 2639 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Cass v. State, 123 So. 3d 1224, 2013 La. LEXIS 2307 (La., 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Cass v. Keith, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44659 (W.D. La., Jan. 30, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 260,683. Honorable John R. Joyce, Pro Tem Judge, Honorable Craig O. Marcotte, Judge.
State v. Cass, 17 So. 3d 486, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1498 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966 (A)(1). He was adjudicated a second felony offender and sentenced to 40 years at hard labor "without benefit," and fined $20,000. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the imposition of a $20,000.00 fine was unconstitutional because he was indigent and unable to pay due to his prison sentence. The court of appeal agreed, but for different reasons. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, the habitual offender statute, did not authorize imposition of a fine, but only provided for enhanced sentences relating to the term of imprisonment. A trial court is without authority to impose a fine under this statute. Thus, because the trial court sentenced defendant under the habitual offender statute, it was without authority to impose a fine. Therefore, although based on different grounds, this assignment of error had merit and defendant's sentence is amended to delete the $20,000.00 fine.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, the sentence was amended, and as amended was affirmed.

Jones v. Southern Natural Gas Co.


No. 46,347-CA, (Consolidated with No. 46,348-CA & No. 46,351-CA), No. 46,348-CA, (Consolidated with No. 46,347-CA & No. 46,351-CA), No. 46,351-CA, (Consolidated with No. 46,347-CA & No. 46,348-CA)

46,347 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/13/11); 63 So. 3d 1080; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 442



April 13, 2011, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ dismissed by Jones v. Southern Natural Gas Co., 70 So. 3d 800, 2011 La. LEXIS 2302 (La., Sept. 23, 2011)
Writ dismissed by Jones v. Southern Natural Gas Co., 75 So. 3d 911, 2011 La. LEXIS 2671 (La., Nov. 4, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by, Costs and fees proceeding at, Sub nomine at Baker v. Tenn. Gas Pipeline Co., 2017 La. App. LEXIS 2074 (La.App. 2 Cir., Nov. 15, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 53,999. Honorable Jay B. McCallum, Judge. Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 2009-4304. Honorable Scott Leehy, Judge. Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Union, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 43,464. Honorable Cynthia T. Woodard, Judge.
Jones v. S. Natural Gas Co., 39 So. 3d 593, 2010 La. LEXIS 1723 (La., July 15, 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants taxpayers appealed judgments of the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln (Louisiana), Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) and Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Union (Louisiana) in favor of plaintiffs-appellees assessors that reversed and vacated a ruling of the Louisiana Tax Commission (LTC) and reinstated certain tax assessments.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers argued, inter alia, that the Louisiana Tax Commission and the district courts erred in placing the burden of proof of obsolescence on the taxpayers. The taxpayers argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 47:2324 imposed a mandatory duty on the assessor, and if the assessor felt the information submitted by the taxpayer was inadequate, the assessor was required to request additional supporting data. The court of appeal disagreed. Under the guidelines, the burden was on the party claiming obsolescence to give the assessor sufficient data to support the claim. There was no basis for shifting the burden of proof: the burden was, and remained, with the taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

State v. Decuir

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vermilion (Louisiana) to manslaughter and was sentenced to 35 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court imposed an excessive sentence under La. Const. art. I, § 20 considering the factual circumstances and history of abuse between defendant and the victim. Specifically, she asserted that she was a 44-year-old mother who had supported her family through a life of abuse; that it was her first felony offense; and that the trial court failed to give adequate weight to the mitigating circumstances. The court of appeal disagreed. The record supported the trial court's conclusion; it reflected a history of mutual physical abuse between defendant and her husband, including a prior instance when defendant shot her husband and another previous incident when defendant attacked him in his sleep. Moreover, the record also reflected that defendant frequently threatened to shoot her husband in the head. Additionally, by entering into the plea agreement defendant reduced her sentencing exposure from life imprisonment to 40 years. Therefore, the sentence did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for the trial court to inform defendant of the prescriptive period for filing for post-conviction relief. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Grace


10-1222


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


10-1222 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/06/11); 61 So. 3d 812; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 408



April 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Grace, 73 So. 3d 382, 2011 La. LEXIS 2550 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Grace v. State, 123 So. 3d 1226, 2013 La. LEXIS 2275 (La., 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Grace v. Warden La. State Penitentiary, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60796 (W.D. La., Mar. 16, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 78232-F. HONORABLE J. LARRY VIDRINE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. AGGRAVATED BURGLARY AND CONSPIRACY TO COMMIT AGGRAVATED BURGLARY SENTENCES AFFIRMED. ARMED ROBBERY AND CONSPIRACY TO COMMIT ARMED ROBBERY SENTENCES VACATED. REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING ON THE ARMED ROBBERY AND CONSPIRACY TO COMMIT ARMED ROBBERY CONVICTIONS, WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana) of two counts of armed robbery, one count of aggravated burglary, two counts of conspiracy to commit armed robbery, and one count of conspiracy to commit aggravated burglary. All sentences were ordered to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions. The court of appeal disagreed. Accomplices committed an aggravated burglary when they entered the victim's house without authorization, and although they arrived after the break-in, the victims were all present in the house. The accomplices intended to commit a felony therein--armed robbery. When they broke into the house, they were already armed with a sawed-off shotgun, and they further armed themselves by stealing a handgun the bedroom. Although the defendant was not physically present in the house, the testimony supported a conclusion that defendant was involved in the commission of the offenses. Defendant drove the accomplices to the house, acted as a lookout and was intended to be the "getaway driver" once the robbery was completed. The accomplice's testimony was sufficient to establish that he, defendant, and another person agreed to commit an armed robbery with the purpose of "getting some money" and that they made an act in furtherance of the conspiracy when they drove to the abandoned house to retrieve the sawed-off shotgun eventually used in the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences for armed robbery and conspiracy to commit armed robbery were vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing on those charges. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Langley

OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for second-degree murder was proper because his double jeopardy rights were not violated and the filing of the motion to recuse the district attorney suspended the running of the prescription; thus, there was no violation of defendant's right to a speedy trial. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed and remanded.

Vicksburg Healthcare, LLC v. State through Dep't of Health & Hospitals


2010 CA 1248


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 1248 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/25/11); 63 So. 3d 205; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 356



March 25, 2011, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Vicksburg Healthcare, LLC v. State, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1580 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NUMBER 571,263, DIV. 24, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE R. MICHAEL CALDWELL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee out-of-state hospital filed an action for declaratory relief and damages against appellant Louisiana Department of Health and Hospitals (DHH). The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted the hospital's motion for partial summary judgment, finding that the DHH's reimbursement methodology was unconstitutional and was applied in a manner that discriminated against the hospital. The DHH appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hospital challenged a rule promulgated by the DHH that reimbursed out-of-state (border) hospitals differently than in-state hospitals that provided inpatient hospital services to Louisiana Medicaid patients. The hospital argued that the reimbursement methodology violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. The court found that the State's role was that of market regulator, which meant that the DHH rule as applied to the hospital was subject to scrutiny under the Commerce Clause. The DHH claimed that its rule was for the purpose of assuring the continued viability for rural hospitals. The court found that it was a protectionist measure and the DHH offered nothing to show that its objective of preserving small rural hospitals could not be accomplished by nondiscriminatory alternatives. Thus, the reimbursement rule was unconstitutional as it applied to the hospital and violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1300.144(A)(3)(b). However, the trial court's declaration that the rule was unconstitutional on its face was error as the evidence was insufficient to show that other border hospitals experienced the discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment and found that the DHH's reimbursement rule as it applied to the hospital was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment as amended.

State v. Harris


2010 KA 0643


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 0643 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/25/11); 63 So. 3d 226; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 367



March 25, 2011, Judgment rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 479288, Division "B". Honorable August J. Hand, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: DENIAL OF THE MOTION TO QUASH REVERSED; MOTION TO QUASH GRANTED; GUILTY PLEA CONVICTION AND SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, which denied his motion to quash the bill of information that charged him with possession of marijuana, second offense under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(C). He argued that the charged offense was not his second offense and that § 40:966 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea that reserved his right to challenge the denial of his motion to quash. Defendant maintained that the instant offense was not punishable as a second offense because it was committed before he was convicted for his prior possession of marijuana offense. He argued that § 40:966(E)(2) should be interpreted as requiring a second offense be committed after the conviction for the first offense. The State argued that a plain reading of § 40:966(E)(2) did not require that the first conviction occur before the commission of the second offense. The court concluded that § 40-966 was not unconstitutionally vague. Pursuant to case law precedent and finding no legislative amendment to the contrary, the court held that defendant could not be guilty of the crime of possession of marijuana, second offense, unless such crime was committed after the conviction for the first offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, granted the motion to quash, vacated defendant's guilty plea conviction and sentence, and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Kimble


2010 KA 1559


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 1559 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/25/11) 62 So. 3d 782; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 366



March 25, 2011, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Kimble, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 798 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 20, 2015)
Writ denied by, As moot State v. Kimble, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 2334 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 18, 2015)
Writ denied by, As moot State v. Kimble, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 2451 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 7, 2015)
Writ denied by State v. Kimble, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 194 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 10, 2016)
Writ denied by, As moot State v. Kimble, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 1505 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 8, 2016)
Writ denied by State v. Kimble, 2017 La. App. LEXIS 677 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NUMBER 06-06-0190, SEC. 2, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE RICHARD D. ANDERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) of aggravated burglary, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60 and armed robbery, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 and was sentenced to thirty years at hard labor and fifty years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence respectively, the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in refusing to permit him to represent himself at trial. The court of appeal disagreed. Defendant filed a pro se motion requesting that he be allowed to act as co-counsel at his trial. The trial court denied the motion without a hearing. Defendant did not re-urge the motion at any point during the trial. Defendant did not unequivocally indicate to the trial court that he wanted to represent himself in this prosecution without the assistance of any counsel. Instead, he requested to be allowed to act as co-counsel, in conjunction with his court-appointed attorney. While the defendant had the right to counsel as well as the right to self-representation, he had no constitutional right to be both represented and representative. Furthermore, defendant did not allege, and the court of appeal did not find, any way in which his defense was prejudiced because defendant did not participate as co-counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Blackledge v. Sol's Pipe & Steel, Inc.


No. 46,148-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,148 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/23/11); 59 So. 3d 564; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 344



March 23, 2011, Judgment rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 2010-1783. Honorable Bernard Scott Leehy, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was working for appellee employer as part of a work-release program when he was injured. He filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits but was granted a stay. He filed a petition for a declaration that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201.4 was unconstitutional. The Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, found it constitutional and dismissed his petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employer filed a motion for sanctions for filing a frivolous appeal. The inmate argued that § 23:1201.4 was not substantially related to any legitimate government interest. He lived in a halfway house, and he argued that his wages, not state funds, paid for his needs. The court found that the majority of the inmate's wages were collected and used to pay for his expenses. The state had an interest in prisoners being successfully integrated back into society. The work-release program helped to promote that interest. The statute encouraged employers to hire convicts, avoided duplicative payments to prisoners, and kept down unnecessary workers' compensation claims, which were all appropriate government objectives. The statute did not violate the equal protection clause or the due process class as it bore a rational relationship to legitimate government interests. The inmate failed to show the statute was unconstitutional on its face.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The court denied the employer's motion for sanctions.

Abundance Square Assocs., L.P. v. Williams


NO. 2010-CA-0324


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0324 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/23/11); 62 So. 3d 261; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 351



March 23, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 26, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2008-2261, DIVISION "K-5". HONORABLE HERBERT A. CADE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, which upheld the assessment of ad valorem tax for 2008 on their two housing developments by defendants, a city and its tax assessor. Plaintiffs had paid the taxes under protest and argued that the properties were exempt pursuant to La. Const. art. VII, § 21(A).


OVERVIEW: The tax assessor testified that improvements on immovable property were exempt from taxation only if the improvements were owned by a public entity or non-profit corporation that used the property for a charitable purposes. The owners were private entities. Upon review, the court found that ownership alone was not determinative of whether the property served a public purpose. Privately-owned property could be dedicated to public use and eligible for tax exempt status. Plaintiffs had entered into agreements to operate 71 of their apartments in their two housing developments as public housing units. The money they derived from the rental of the public housing units was used strictly for the operation and maintenance costs of those units. Plaintiffs did not earn a profit on those units. The court held that to the extent plaintiffs were contractually and legally obligated to operate and maintain the units as public housing, those units had been dedicated to public use, served a public purpose, and thus, were clearly exempt from ad valorem taxes under La. Const. art. VII, § 21(A).


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment and granted a return of the ad valorem taxes paid under protest on the 71 public housing units in plaintiffs' two housing developments. To the extent they were denied a refund on the remaining units, the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Odoms


NO. 2010-KA-1278


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-1278 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/16/11); 62 So. 3d 252; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 329



March 16, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 19, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Odoms, 2011 La. LEXIS 2451 (La., Oct. 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 497-525, SECTION "K". HONORABLE ARTHUR HUNTER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded nolo contendere in the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish (Louisiana) to the charge of possession of marijuana, second offense in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E) reserving his right to appeal the denial of his subsequently filed written motion to quash the bill of information. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to quash the bill of information based upon his claim that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E), was unconstitutional. He argued that the United State Supreme Court's ruling in Apprendi v. New Jersey mandated a finding that § 40:966(E) was unconstitutional because the statute allowed the State to increase the maximum sentence to which he was exposed based upon a prior misdemeanor conviction for which he was not entitled to a jury trial. The court of appeal disagreed. The Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments, U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV, did not preclude the sentence-enhancing use, against an adult, of a prior valid, fair, and reliable conviction of a misdemeanor, obtained as an adult, where the misdemeanor proceeding included all the constitutional protections applicable to such proceedings, even though these protections do not include the right to trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Stipe


10-877


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


10-877 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/09/11); 59 So. 3d 480; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 300



March 9, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NOS. 18223-06 AND 18225-06. HONORABLE ALVIN TURNER, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Stipe, 30 So. 3d 287, 2010 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 11 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the 14th Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Lousiana), which convicted him of one charge of carjacking under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.2 and one charge of armed robbery with the use of a firearm under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:64, 14:64.3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in imposing an unconstitutionally excessive sentence. First, he argued that the offenses were essentially part of a common scheme or plan because they evidently occurred within a relatively short period of time and that under La. Code Crim. P. art. 883, the trial court erred in not giving specific reasons for ordering the sentences to run consecutively. Second, he argued that because the sentence was imposed consecutively to a life sentence that there was no chance of defendant's release during his natural life even if his life sentence was commuted. Defendant argued that such a sentence constituted the purposeless and needless imposition of pain and suffering prohibited by La. Const. art. 1, § 20. The court held that defendant pointed to no evidence in the record to support his claim that the offenses were part of a common scheme or plan other than a bare assertion that the offenses occurred within a relatively short period of time and that imprisonment itself was not necessarily cruel and unusual even if the term of imprisonment was lengthy or if the sentences were imposed consecutively.


OUTCOME: The decision was upheld but remanded with instructions to stipulate that the five-year sentence for the use of a firearm enhancement be served without hard labor.

Rent-A-Center E., Inc. v. Lincoln Parish Sales

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


46,054 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/09/11); 60 So. 3d 95; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 301



March 9, 2011, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Rent-A-Center East, Inc. v. Lincoln Parish Sales & Use Tax Comm'n, 63 So. 3d 985, 2011 La. LEXIS 1366 (La., May 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 52447. Honorable Jay B. McCallum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED; AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sales and use tax commission assessed penalties for nonpayment of sales taxes against plaintiff taxpayer. The taxpayer paid the amount due under protest and filed suit against the commission, requesting a refund. The Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, entered summary judgment for the commission. The taxpayer sought review, and the commission sought additional attorney's fees for work done on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was in the business of selling and leasing various articles of tangible property to customers. When entering a lease, a customer could purchase a liability damage waiver (LDW). The commission found that sales tax was due on the LDW sales, and the trial court agreed. The trial court also ordered the taxpayer to pay the commission attorney's fees. Upon review, the court found that the proceeds derived from the LDW sales was subject to the sales tax under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:302(B)(1) as they were derived from the lease or rental of tangible personal property. A penalty was properly assessed against the taxpayer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1602(A) as it failed to remit the taxes it owed. The taxpayer's payment of the taxes under protest was not a timely payment that avoided its liability for attorney's fees under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1512. La. Const. art. VII, § 3(A) did not prohibit the award of attorney's fees to the commission. As the commission incurred additional expenses on appeal, the court awarded additional attorney's fees and found $ 2,500 to be a reasonable amount.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment to award additional attorney's fees for work done on appeal and affirmed the judgment as amended.

State v. Phillips


NO. 2010-KA-0582


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0582 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/17/77); 61 So. 3d 130; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 235



February 17, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 25, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Phillips, 71 So. 3d 311, 2011 La. LEXIS 2334 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Phillips v. State, 118 So. 3d 1119, 2013 La. LEXIS 1738 (La., 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Phillips v. Cain, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125070 (E.D. La., Sept. 8, 2014)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Phillips v. State, 149 So. 3d 789, 2014 La. LEXIS 2149 (La., 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Phillips v. State, 2015 La. LEXIS 1239 (La., June 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 486-174, SECTION "E". Honorable Keva M. Landrum-Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court for Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of one count of purse snatching. Defendant was sentenced to serve ten years at hard labor concurrently with any other sentence he may be serving. The defendant was subsequently adjudicated a third felony offender and resentenced pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 to serve life imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the district court abused its discretion when it sentenced him to the life sentence mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 without any inquiry as to whether the sentence was excessive under the facts of the case as required by State v. Dorthey. The court of appeals disagreed. None of the mitigating factors defendant presented overwhelmed the presumption that the legislatively-mandated sentence was appropriate. His two prior convictions were for simple robbery and armed robbery. In the case at hand, the defendant implied that he had a weapon and threatened to shoot the victims. A life sentence was the minimum which could be imposed on the defendant under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(2)(b)(i)(ii) because the instant felony conviction and two of his prior felony convictions were crimes of violence as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13). Thus, despite his attempt to present mitigating factors to the court, the defendant failed to provide substantial evidence that exceptional circumstances justified a downward departure from the mandatory term of life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Landry


NO. 2010-KA-1225


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-1225 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/16/11); 60 So. 3d 714; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 226



February 16, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 25, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Landry, 2011 La. LEXIS 2213 (La., Sept. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 489-569, SECTION "A". Honorable Laurie A. White, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant, charged with prostitution, argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:82C was unconstitutional in that it allowed the State to increase the maximum sentence to which she was exposed based upon at least one prior misdemeanor conviction for which she was not entitled to a jury trial. The court held that § 14:82C was not unconstitutional because the non-jury trial for the first offense included all the constitutional protections applicable to misdemeanors.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Farmer's Seafood Co. v. State


2010 CA 1746


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 1746 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/11); 56 So. 3d 1263; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 185



February 14, 2011, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by, Motion granted by Farmer's Seafood Co. v. State, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 1044 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 8, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 582,119, Division "D". Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.
Farmer's Seafood Co. v. State through Dep't of Pub. Safety, Office of State Police, 44 So. 3d 676, 2010 La. LEXIS 1826 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A contractor supplied seafood to riverboat casinos. The Louisiana Gaming Control Board found that the contractor employed a convicted felon, who was unsuitable under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:28. The court upheld a preliminary injunction against the Board from enforcing § 27:28 as unconstitutional under the separation of powers principle because the statutory scheme did not prescribe sufficient standards to guide the Board in determining who was or should be suitable. La. Admin. Code tit. XIII, § 2901(B) apparently exceeded and was inconsistent with the legislature's authorization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court granting a preliminary injunction enjoining and restraining the Board and the State Police from proceeding with the administrative actions proposed against the contractor. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

894 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gandy


No. 45,947-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,947 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/02/11); 57 So. 3d 1163; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 125



February 2, 2011, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Gandy, 2011 La. LEXIS 2333 (La., Oct. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 279,610. Honorable Michael A. Pitman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.3. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.3 The court of appeals disagreed. It was undisputed that defendant and the victim had an intimate relationship, and that defendant had permission to enter the victim's home on prior occasions. Permission to enter one day, however, did not give defendant carte blanche authorization to enter any time he wished. It was the victim's uncontradicted testimony that on the date of the incident she repeatedly denied defendant entry into her home and repeatedly asked him to leave her property. Nevertheless, defendant entered the home and forced his way into the victim's bathroom while she was bathing. Regardless of whether defendant let himself in, or, as defendant testified, the victim's ten-year-old son opened the door for him, it was clear that there was sufficient evidence for the jury to conclude that defendant entered the victim's home without the consent of a person with the authority and/or capacity to consent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Boyer


10-693 c/w 10-694


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


10-693(La.App. 3 Cir. 02/02/11); 56 So. 3d 1119; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 137



February 2, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Boyer, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 327 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 16, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Boyer v. Louisiana, 133 S. Ct. 420, 184 L. Ed. 2d 252, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 7811 (U.S., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Boyer v. Louisiana, 133 S. Ct. 1702, 185 L. Ed. 2d 774, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 3518 (U.S., 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Boyer v. Cain, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41122 (W.D. La., Jan. 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 14005-02. HONORABLE G. MICHAEL CANADAY, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Boyer, 56 So. 3d 1162, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 119 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which convicted and sentenced him for second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and armed robbery with a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:64 and 14:64.3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences for second-degree murder and armed robbery with a firearm, but the appellate court affirmed, stating in part that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it refused to allow defendant to question a witness about an incident which did not result in a pending charge or conviction and where there was no prospect of prosecution. Further, any relevance of the domestic abuse complaint was substantially outweighed by the possibility of prejudice, confusion of the issue, or misleading of the jury. Defendant's maximum sentence of 99 years, plus 5 years for a total of one 104 years at hard labor was proper because he purposefully killed the victim by putting the gun to the victim's head and firing at least two times. Further, during defendant's incarceration, he was charged with criminal damage to property and taking contraband into a penal institution. The record also showed that during his detention, defendant committed attempted aggravated escape and battery on a police officer. He was disciplined more than 40 times while incarcerated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Domino


NO. 10-KA-661


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


10-661 (La.App. 5 Cir. 1/25/11); 60 So. 3d 659; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 88



January 25, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 15, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 08-1748, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE GLENN B. ANSARDI, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana sought review of a decision of the 24th Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash. Defendant had been charged with driving while intoxicated (DWI), third offense, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(A)(D).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had filed a motion to quash the bill of information that alleged the trial judge and the attorney failed to sign the waiver of rights form in his first predicate offense. Defendant then filed a supplemental motion in which he argued that a review of the transcript demonstrated his plea was not voluntarily or knowingly entered. After a hearing was held, the trial court granted defendant's motion to quash the first DWI predicate, finding that the State did not prove a valid waiver of his rights. The court overruled the decision. The transcript of the first predicate conviction showed that defendant, who was unrepresented, knowingly and intelligently waived his right to counsel before pleading guilty to the first predicate DWI. According to the transcript, defendant appeared in person. At the beginning of the proceeding, the trial judge confirmed defendant's date of birth and also confirmed his social security number and driver's license number. The judge also confirmed that defendant had a 12th grade education. He explained that defendant was charged with driving while intoxicated on a certain date and was pleading guilty. Defendant agreed that the judge was correct.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded.

State v. Vincent


NO. 2010-KA-0764


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0764 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/19/11); 56 So. 3d 408; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 34



January 19, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 24, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Vincent, 63 So. 3d 1038, 2011 La. LEXIS 1527 (La., June 17, 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Vincent v. State, 118 So. 3d 1112, 2013 La. LEXIS 1700 (La., July 31, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Vincent v. State, 184 So. 3d 678, 2016 La. LEXIS 204 (La., Feb. 19, 2016)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 486-968, SECTION "I". Honorable Karen K. Herman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A 20-year sentence for a fourth felony offender's conviction for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:68.4, was not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20, where defendant was subject to a sentencing range of twenty years to life, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i), and no downward departure of the mandatory minimum sentence was justified. Further, it would have been an exercise in futility for the trial court to have articulated the sentencing factors of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 because the sentence was mandatory.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.
