State v. Mason


NO. 10-KA-284


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


10-284 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/11/11); 59 So. 3d 419; 2011 La. App. LEXIS 17



January 11, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 15, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Mason, 64 So. 3d 216, 2011 La. LEXIS 1636 (La., June 24, 2011)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Writ denied by State ex rel. Mason v. State, 148 So. 3d 944, 2014 La. LEXIS 2091 (La., Sept. 19, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Mason v. Vannoy, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28649 (E.D. La., Feb. 9, 2015)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Mason v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 2620 (La., Nov. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-368, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE J. STERLING SNOWDY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of armed robbery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 and one count of attempted armed robbery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27 and 14:64. The Fortieth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist, Louisiana, sentenced him to 55 years imprisonment for the armed robbery conviction and 50 years imprisonment for the attempted armed robbery with the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to establish that he was the one who committed the crimes. The eyewitnesses did not see the faces of the perpetrators because their faces and heads were covered. However, there was surveillance video and one of the videos included sound. The vehicle that was used in the commission of the crimes was found and had clothing in it like that worn by the perpetrators in the videos. Defendant's DNA profile was consistent with DNA found on a shirt recovered from the car. Defendant's fingerprints were found in and on the car. The court concluded that the evidence of defendant's identity negated any possibility of misidentification. Defendant argued that his sentences were excessive given his age. The court found that defendant was not an individual without a criminal history. Defendant's sentence for armed robbery was not excessive under the circumstances of the case. It was within the statutory range. However, the court found that the 50 year sentence for attempted armed robbery was illegal as it was beyond the maximum allowed under §§ 14:64 and 14:27.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the 55-year sentence for armed robbery. The court vacated defendant's 50-year sentence for attempted armed robbery and remanded for resentencing.

 

900 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Bossier Parish Police Jury


No. 45, 639-CA, No. 45, 829-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45 639 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/15/10); 56 So. 3d 275; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1751



December 15, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Anderson v. Bossier Parish Police Jury, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 2782 (La.App. 2 Cir., Nov. 19, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 130,698 & 130,699. Honorable Parker Self and Michael O. Craig, Judges.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, plaintiff property owners appealed from judgments of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana), holding that their claims against defendants, the parish police jury, the office of the parish engineer, and the engineer (collectively, the police jury), challenging an ordinance placing portions of their property in a floodway, had prescribed pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492.


OVERVIEW: In enacting the ordinance at issue, the police jury adopted recommendations by the Federal Emergency Management Agency and placed portions of the owners' property in the floodway of the Red Chute Bayou rather than in the flood zone, as they were previously classified. The property owners alleged that because of the new classification, encroachments were prohibited, including fill, new construction, substantial improvements, and other developments. The property owners clearly alleged a "taking" in their pleadings and, thus, the three-year prescriptive period of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5111, rather than the one-year period of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492, was applicable for those claims. The event that triggered the running of prescription was the passage of the ordinance placing the property in the floodway. The ordinance became effective less than one year before the property owners filed their action. Accordingly, the claims had not prescribed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments and remanded the matters for further proceedings.

State v. Winslow


No. 45,414-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,414 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/15/10); 55 So. 3d 910; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1737



December 15, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Winslow, 63 So. 3d 1033, 2011 La. LEXIS 1516 (La., June 17, 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Winslow v. State, 135 So. 3d 611, 2014 La. LEXIS 735 (La., Mar. 21, 2014)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Winslow v. State, 152 So. 3d 890, 2014 La. LEXIS 2733 (La., Nov. 21, 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Winslow v. State, 184 So. 3d 15, 2016 La. LEXIS 92 (La., Jan. 25, 2016)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Winslow v. Cain, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 158999 (W.D. La., May 15, 2017)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Winslow v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1634 (La., Aug. 4, 2017)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Winslow v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1678 (La., Aug. 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 271,588. Honorable John Joyce, Judge, Honorable Craig O. Marcotte, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, of distribution of marijuana, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1)(a). He was adjudicated a fourth felony offender and sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without parole, probation, or suspension. After an appeal and remand, defendant was resentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefits. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient. The court noted that the testimony of a single undercover police officer was sufficient to convict. In this case, an undercover officer testified that defendant asked him what he wanted and told him that he could get him two dime bags of marijuana; defendant then left to get the marijuana, returned, and handed the marijuana to the officer in exchange for $ 25. A sergeant testified that he heard the transaction over the officer's audio transmitting device and saw the hand-to-hand exchange. This evidence was sufficient. The State's use of an arrest report containing defendant's fingerprint, in combination with certified minutes and a bill of information, was sufficient to prove that defendant was the same person convicted of simple burglary in 1994. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(F) did not require any specific type of evidence at a habitual offender hearing; prior convictions could be proved by any competent evidence. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(ii), defendant's life sentence was mandatory. Therefore, the trial court was not required to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1.


OUTCOME: The defendant's conviction, adjudication as a fourth felony offender, and sentence were affirmed.

 

902 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Materre


NO. 2009-KA-1666


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-1666 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/08/10); 53 So. 3d 615; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1705



December 8, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 10, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Materre, 2011 La. LEXIS 1928 (La., Sept. 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 472-116, SECTION "C". HONORABLE BENEDICT J. WILLARD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), after he was charged with second degree murder and armed robbery but found guilty by a jury of negligent homicide. On the State's information charging defendant as a fourth felony offender, the trial court resentenced defendant to seventy-five years at hard labor under Louisiana's Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction and that his sentence under the Habitual Offender Law was unconstitutionally excessive under the Eighth Amendment and La. Const. art. I, § 20 when applied to the crime of negligent homicide. The court held that the jury chose to give greater weight to the testimony of the State's witnesses and circumstantial evidence such as defendant's avoidance of police after the shooting than it gave to defendant's statement that the victim was shot by a person in a passing car. While the trial judge did not articulate the factual basis for the sentence and no comparable sentences for a quadruple offender convicted of negligent homicide could be found, imposition of the maximum sentence was not excessive in light of the facts of the case and defendant's extensive and violent 15-year criminal history that included first-degree robbery (reduced from an initial charge of armed robbery, a crime of violence) and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. Failure of the sentencing court to enumerate the factors listed in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 did not require remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

903 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Monroe


NO. 2010-KA-0194


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0194 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/08/10); 53 So. 3d 626; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1708



December 8, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 10, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Monroe, 2011 La. LEXIS 1233 (La., May 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 479-470, SECTION "I". HONORABLE KAREN K. HERMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of one count of sexual battery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.43.1, and sentenced him to 10 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three counts of sexual battery. He was convicted of one count. The victim was a 13-year-old girl. On appeal, he claimed that his conviction on count two was duplicitous of his acquittal on count one. The court found that neither the Blockburger test nor the Louisiana "same evidence" rule supported his assertion of double jeopardy under La. Const. art. 1, § 15 and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 591. Defendant was charged with committing the crime of sexual battery on three distinct occasions, each punishable separately. Further, the testimony at trial was sufficient to prove that he intentionally engaged in acts wherein his genitals touched the 13-year-old, non-spouse victim. The victim testified that she had consensual sexual intercourse with him on three occasions in 2006, when she was only 13 years old. The State introduced a copy of defendant's birth certificate, which proved that he was more than three years older than the victim at the time of the offenses. Finally, defendant's sentence was not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20. In sentencing him, the trial judge noted that he was an adult taking advantage of an impressionable child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

904 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mueller


NO.2010-KA-0710


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0882 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/08/10); 53 So. 3d 677; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1706



December 8, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 10, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 484-248, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of failure to register as a sex offender between October 8, 2008 and January 8, 2009, after prior convictions for indecent behavior on February 27, 1998 in Oklahoma and third-degree sexual abuse on January 28, 2000 in Iowa, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 and sentencing him to 10 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that defendant was required to register as a sex offender under § 15:542 because his Oklahoma and Iowa convictions were equivalent to Louisiana statutes that required registration; Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1021(A)(1) was equivalent to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81, and Iowa Code § 709.4(1) was equivalent to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:42, 14:42.1. There was no support for defendant's claims that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 applied only to sex offenses against minors or that sex offenders from other states were free from a duty to register in Louisiana if their sex offender convictions in those other states were not subject to registration in those states. Defendant's claim of improper venue was not reviewable because he failed to file a pretrial motion to quash as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 615. The court held that defendant's maximum 10-year sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive given defendant's prior criminal history, which included multiple prior felony convictions including two sex crimes, defendant's defiance in complying with conditions of his probation, and his general recidivist history.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

905 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morrison


No. 45,620-KA, No. 45,621-KA (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,650 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/24/10); 55 So. 3d 856; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1602



November 24, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 33,229 and 33,229A. Honorable Jimmy C. Teat, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson (Louisiana), which convicted her of aggravated rape and aggravated oral sexual battery. She received concurrent sentences of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence on the rape conviction and 20 years at hard labor for the battery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her convictions and sentences for aggravated rape in violation of former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:24 and aggravated oral sexual battery in violation of former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.4 (repealed 2001). The bill of indictment alleged that defendant aided and abetted her husband in his having vaginal intercourse with the victim and that defendant had oral sex with the victim. The victim was a nine-year-old girl whose aunt was a family friend. The appellate court affirmed, stating that from the evidence, the jury could have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that penetration occurred during the perpetrator's sexual intercourse with the child with defendant's voluntary participation. Additionally, the record did not support her justification claim. While defendant's testimony supported her contention that she suffered abuse at the hands of her husband, the evidence did not show that at the time she committed either offense she was in imminent peril of great bodily harm, or that she reasonably believed herself or others to have been in such danger.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

906 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic


09-439


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-439 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/17/10); 51 So. 3d 874; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1583



November 17, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic, 57 So. 3d 307, 2011 La. LEXIS 694 (La., 2011)
Vacated by, En banc, Remanded by Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic, 57 So. 3d 307, 2011 La. LEXIS 945 (La., 2011)
Vacated by, En banc, Remanded by Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic, 57 So. 3d 308, 2011 La. LEXIS 946 (La., 2011)
On reconsideration by, En banc, Adhered to Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1013 (La.App. 3 Cir., Aug. 31, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2005-3907. HONORABLE CLAYTON DAVIS, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; EXCEPTION OF RES JUDICATA DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) of the Medical Malpractice Act (MMA) to substantially reduce a jury's general damage award. Plaintiffs, parents and their minor child, appealed. The Louisiana Patients' Compensation Fund (PCF) also appealed and defendant nurse practitioner filed a peremptory exception of res judicata.


OVERVIEW: The Medical Review Panel and the jury found that the nurse practitioner committed malpractice. The jury a general damage award of $ 6,233,000, which included past medical expenses and judicial interest on the expenses. The trial court, applying the MMA's damages cap, reduced the award to $ 500,000. The MMA's cap on general damage awards unconstitutionally disadvantage and discriminated against the child and her parents because of the severity of the child's physical condition when compared to other malpractice victims who received full recovery for their injuries. Further, the State failed to present sufficient evidence to show that any reasonable basis existed to continue such discrimination by expanding the MMA's limitation on general tort liability to include nurse practitioners. Accordingly, the MMA's cap, when used to limit nurse practitioners' general liability for damages cause to severely or catastrophically injured victims, unconstitutionally violated the Equal Protection Clause of La. Const. art. I, § 3. Further, past medical expenses were authorized under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43(B). Finally, there was no merit in the peremptory exception of res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court denied the exception of res judicata. It affirmed the award of past medical expenses and judicial interest, and reversed that portion of the judgment that reduced the jury's general damage award. The court reinstated the jury's award of damages.

 

907 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Silver Dollar Liquor, Inc. v. Red River Parish Police Jury


No. 45,637-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,637 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/17/10); 56 So. 3d 265; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1584



November 17, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Silver Dollar Liquor, Inc. v. Red River Parish Police Jury, 57 So. 3d 322, 2011 La. LEXIS 495 (La., 2011)
Affirmed by Silver Dollar Liquor, Inc. v. Red River Parish Police Jury, 2011 La. LEXIS 1909 (La., Sept. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Red River, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 34,883. Honorable Fred C. Sexton, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a liquor store owner, brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant police jury in the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Red River, Louisiana, seeking to declare a local police jury ordinance invalid. The trial court invalidated the local ordinance, and the police jury appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a 1939 election regarding prohibition, the parish was voted "dry." This changed in 1974 with a Louisiana Supreme Court holding that the effect of such earlier prohibition elections was superseded by 1950 legislation requiring local option elections on a ward basis for separate areas throughout a parish. In 1975, the police jury enacted a new ordinance prohibiting Sunday sales of alcohol in District 6. The trial court declared the ordinance invalid on the grounds that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191 required a vote of the people authorizing the closing of businesses on Sunday, and no such election had occurred. The court held that even assuming that the election required under § 51:191 limited the police jury's power to enact such ordinances, the 1986 legislation did not operate to repeal all existing local ordinances which prohibited the Sunday sales of alcohol. When the legislature removed itself from the regulation of Sunday business enterprise in 1986 without drawing back the police jury's authority under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493 for Sunday closing laws for alcohol, the ordinance retained its independent force.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the trial court.

 

908 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Green


NO. 2010-KA-0008


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0008 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/17/10); 52 So. 3d 253; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1593



November 17, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 27, 2011.
Post-conviction proceeding at, Writ denied by State ex rel. Green v. State, 99 So. 3d 670, 2012 La. LEXIS 3048 (La., 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Green v. Cain, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16098 (E.D. La., Jan. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 470-137, SECTION "J". HONORABLE DARRYL A. DERBIGNY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of attempted forcible rape in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana). The district court found him to be a third felony offender, denied defendant's motion to consider a sentence other than life imprisonment, and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to declare La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782(A) unconstitutional to the extent that it allowed for a non-unanimous verdict in non-capital felony cases. Because defendant did not request that the jury be polled, and therefore did not make a record as to whether the verdict was non-unanimous, defendant lacked standing to raise the issue. The court held that, given its comments, the trial court erroneously believed that it had no discretion and that it could not impose any sentence other than the life sentence mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Because the trial court had discretion to impose a sentence of less than the mandatory minimum if defendant could prove that he was exceptional, remand was required. The court held that a guilty plea form in a prior conviction signed by both defendant and his counsel, along with a minute entry showing that defendant was represented by counsel and was interrogated as to his constitutional rights, was sufficient to establish the existence of the prior guilty plea as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence but remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing at which defendant could present evidence that he was an exceptional case entitled to be sentenced to less than the mandatory minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law.

 

909 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


NO. 2010 KA 1592


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 1592 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/10/10); 52 So. 3d 210; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1548



November 10, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Lee, 2011 La. LEXIS 1921 (La., Sept. 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 32nd Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne State of Louisiana. District Court No. 556,154. The Honorable George Larke, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT GRANTING MOTION TO QUASH REVERSED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by grand jury indictment with two counts of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30. The State challenged an order of the 32nd Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne State of Louisiana, which granted defendant's motion to quash the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Reading the indictment as a whole, the court of appeal found that the indictment complied with the constitutional requirement that defendant be informed of the nature and cause of the accusation against him, La. Const. art. I, § 13. The use of the short-form indictment provided by law complied with the constitutional requirement of La. Const. art. I, § 13. The indictment included the language "unlawfully kill in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30." Said language, which broadly encompassed first degree murder, and the inclusion of the statutory citation for first degree murder, unmistakably conveyed the charges returned in the case. The indorsement of the foreman of the grand jury setting out the charges of first degree murder for which a true bill was found was as much a part of the indictment as the remainder of the document. The State had authority to amend the indictment. In accordance with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 487, the district attorney had complete authority to amend indictment, both as to form and substance, at any time before trial. Because defendant was properly informed of the charges, pretrial amendment of the indictment would not be prejudicial to him.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal reversed the trial court's ruling quashing the indictment and remand the matter for further proceedings.

 

910 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


NO. 10-KA-265


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


10 265 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/09/10); 54 So. 3d 98; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1551



November 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 16, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-1244, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE ELLEN S. KOVACH, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Williams, 918 So. 2d 466, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2481 (La.App. 5 Cir., Nov. 29, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 2004, a jury in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, found defendant guilty, of the aggravated rape of A.L. and the sexual battery of B.B. After two appeals, the district court resentenced defendant for the rape to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, and imprisonment at hard labor for ten years, consecutive, for the battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had sex with his stepdaughter from the time she was eight or nine years old until she was approximately twelve years old (from 1998 until 2003). Defendant sexually touched his ex-wife's sister from the time she was eight years old until she was twelve years old (from 1988 until 1992). Defendant argued that he received an illegal sentence on the aggravated rape count because the trial judge referred to count one as "aggravated battery" when she sentenced him, rather than aggravated rape. The court disagreed, deciding that the trial judge simply inadvertently said battery instead of rape. The imposed sentence of life imprisonment did not fall within the sentencing range for aggravated battery, only aggravated rape. Defendant also argued that his consecutive sentences were constitutionally excessive. The court held that because defendant failed to explicitly state an objection to the consecutive nature of the sentences, he was not entitled to review of that issue. Defendant failed to prove any unusual circumstances warranting a departure from the mandatory minimum sentence for aggravated rape, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences for his convictions of aggravated rape and sexual battery were affirmed. The matter was remanded for the corrections of the minute entry and for the trial court to properly advise defendant of the prescriptive period for filing a petition for post-conviction relief.

State v. Thomas


NO. 10-KA-220


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


10-220 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/09/10); 54 So. 3d 678; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1549



November 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 16, 2011.
Review denied by State v. Thomas, 62 So. 3d 89, 2011 La. LEXIS 1001 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State v. Thomas, 63 So. 3d 974, 2011 La. LEXIS 1414 (La., 2011)
Writ dismissed by State ex rel. Thomas v. State, 2016 La. LEXIS 783 (La., Apr. 4, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 08-2003, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE ELLEN S. KOVACH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery, attempted armed robbery, and aggravated battery by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, following the denial of his motion to quash the bill of information. His post-trial motions were denied. He was sentenced to a total effective sentence of 110 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed. A separate appeal was pending on the habitual offender proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782(A) was constitutional. The state's highest court had followed the United States Supreme Court's holding that non-unanimous 12-person jury verdicts were constitutional. The appellate court was not at liberty to ignore the controlling jurisprudence of superior courts. The trial court properly denied defendant's proposed jury charges. The first request was likely to confuse the jury. The general jury charges informed the jury of its option to return a responsive verdict. Defendant did not offer any jurisprudence to support his third proposed charge. That charge, too, was sufficiently covered in the general charge. Defendant's sentence on the aggravated battery count was illegally lenient. The appellate court exercised its discretion not to correct the illegal sentence and impose the fine required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34. While the commitment reflected that defendant was properly advised of the prescriptive period for filing post-conviction relief under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8, the transcript reflected that defendant received an incomplete advisal. The error was corrected.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan


NO. 09-CA-620


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-620 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/09/10); 53 So. 3d 492; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1554



November 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 14, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1806 (La.App. 5 Cir., Dec. 14, 2010)
Writ granted by Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan, 61 So. 3d 673, 2011 La. LEXIS 875 (La., Apr. 8, 2011)
Writ denied by Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan, 61 So. 3d 687, 2011 La. LEXIS 930 (La., Apr. 8, 2011)
Reversed by Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan, 79 So. 3d 987, 2011 La. LEXIS 3014 (La., Dec. 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 625-567, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.
Oubre v. 927 So. 2d 297, 2006 La. LEXIS 1531 (La., May 1, 2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed three rulings of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff and class representative insureds who alleged that the insurer failed to comply with its statutory duty under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:658(A)(3) to initiate loss adjustment in a timely manner and thus was liable for statutory penalties provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220.


OVERVIEW: A class was certified and affirmed for insureds whose loss adjustment after two hurricanes was not begun by the insurer within thirty days after they notified the insurer of their loss. The court reversed the blanket assessment of a minimum penalty of $ 5,000 for each member of three sub-groups within the class. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:658(A)(3) (renumbered as La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1892) provided that an insurer had to initiate loss adjustment of a property damage claim within thirty days after notification of loss by the claimant or be subject to penalties provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220 (renumbered as La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1973). However, before subjecting the insurer to penalties for failing to initiate loss adjustment in a timely manner, a finding had to be made that the insurer breached the duty of good faith. Information before the trial court included dates of claims and dates of insurer reports on the claims but not information on what the insurer did between those dates. On the other hand, there was substantial evidence of unusual circumstances following two hurricanes which may have rendered the insurer unable to meet time limits for adjusting claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court and remand the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Dillard


No. 45,633-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,633 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/03/10); 55 So. 3d 56; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1513



November 3, 2010, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 29, 2011.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Dillard v. State, 75 So. 3d 454, 2011 La. LEXIS 2779 (La., Nov. 18, 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Dillard v. State, 138 So. 3d 618, 2014 La. LEXIS 948 (La., Apr. 17, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Dillard v. Cain, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 158995 (W.D. La., May 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 266,095. Honorable Michael A. Pitman, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of first-degree robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.1, adjudicated him a second felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and sentenced him to 60 years in prison at hard labor without benefits.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for first-degree robbery, but the appellate court affirmed. The evidence was sufficient because the manager of the store identified defendant and the testimony of one witness, if believed by the jury, was sufficient to support a finding of guilt. Further, statements by a customer, who was deceased at the time of the trial, qualified under the present sense impression exception to the hearsay rule, La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803(1), because the only statements that were permitted to be introduced concerned what the customer said to the officer when she flagged him down and described the man that she had followed from the store, and his location. Defendant's double-jeopardy rights were not violated by the third trial taking place because he moved for both mistrials; the actions of the State in failing to provide the defense attorney with the reports in question was simply negligence, not intentional; and defendant was not prejudiced by the mistrials.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jones


NO. 10-KA-281


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


10-281 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/26/10); 51 So. 3d 792; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1432



October 26, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 13, 2011.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Jones v. McCain, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 36280 (E.D. La., Jan. 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-7141, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3, distributing cocaine within 1,000 feet of a church. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, sentenced him to 15 years without probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant sought review of his sentence. Defendant's appellate counsel filed a motion to withdraw.


OVERVIEW: The court allowed defendant's counsel to withdraw as it agreed with her assertion that there were no non-frivolous issues to be raised on appeal. In reviewing defendant's sentence, the court found that there were two errors that made his original sentence illegally lenient. The trial court found the sentence range pursuant to § 40:981.3 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967 to be 5 to 30 years. However, the range under those statutes was 2 to 45 years. The incorrect calculation affected the calculation of his enhanced sentencing range under the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. As a second felony offender, defendant faced a sentencing range of 22.5 to 90 years. Thus, he received a sentence that was 7.5 years less than the mandatory minimum term. While the court had the authority to correct the sentence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 882, even though he entered a plea agreement, it declined to do so as defendant was indigent. The trial court also failed to impose the mandatory fine of $50,000 as required by § 40:981.3 and § 40:967, but the court found that failure harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court granted appellate defense counsel's motion to withdraw. The court advised defendant that any application for post-conviction relief could not be filed more than 2 years after the judgment of conviction and sentence have become final under the provisions of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 914 or 922.

State v. Declouet


NO. 09-KA-1046


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-1046 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/12/10); 52 So. 3d 89; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1372



October 12, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 13, 2011.
Writ denied by State v. Declouet, 61 So. 3d 681, 2011 La. LEXIS 925 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Declouet v. State, 2013 La. LEXIS 1198 (La., May 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-1540, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE GLENN B. ANSARDI, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of three counts of armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, and which sentenced him to an enhanced sentence of 49 1/2 years' imprisonment at hard labor on count one, in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and 22 years on the other two counts.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that counsel was ineffective for failing to request a jury instruction as to accomplice testimony; the evidence presented at trial materially corroborated the accomplice testimony, so a "great caution" instruction was not required. The record supported the sentence imposed because defendant, a second felony offender, and his two accomplices, targeted and robbed the owner and clients of a business and acted without provocation; in committing the robbery, the perpetrators engaged in a physical struggle with at least one of the victims and held the victims at gunpoint, bound them with duct tape, took their cell phones and money and emptied the studio of equipment, and used one of the victim's vehicles as a getaway car. The perpetrators' use of firearms created a risk of death or great bodily harm. Defendant failed to clearly and convincingly show that the mandatory minimum sentence for him as a second felony offender was excessive. The court found error patent, however, because defendant's sentences for armed robbery were considered indeterminate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing.

State v. Anderson


10-0256


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


10-0256 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/06/10); 48 So. 3d 1202; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1339



October 6, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Anderson, 2011 La. LEXIS 660 (La., Mar. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. CR-120075. HONORABLE JOHN DAMIAN TRAHAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which adjudicated him as a habitual offender for his convictions for theft of a firearm, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67.15, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, for which he was sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court based its adjudication of defendant as a third felony habitual offender on the factual conclusion that the state had established that defendant was the same individual who had been convicted of the predicate offenses of armed robbery, first degree robbery and that he was the same individual who had been convicted of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. The appellate court affirmed, finding that defendant had to argue to the supreme court that he did not have fair notice that his sentence for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon was subject to enhancement under the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The state did not improperly use the same predicate offenses to establish he was an habitual offender that it used to establish that he was a convicted felon in possession of a firearm; the only predicate offense used to support defendant's conviction on that charge was his 2002 conviction for first degree robbery. Defendant's speedy trial rights had not been violated. The sentence imposed was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication and sentence, but it remanded the matter for correction of the trial court minutes of the adjudication proceedings.

Fulmer v. State


NO. 2010-CA-0088


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0088 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/06/10); 50 So. 3d 843; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1360



October 6, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 22, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Fulmer v. State, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1638 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 22, 2010)
Writ granted by, Review granted by Fulmer v. State, 57 So. 3d 322, 2011 La. LEXIS 1263 (La., 2011)
Affirmed by Fulmer v. Dep't of Wildlife & Fisheries, 2011 La. LEXIS 1591 (La., July 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM 25TH JDC, PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES. NO. 51-232, DIVISION "B". Honorable Joy Cossich Lobrano, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an injured employee, appealed a decision from the 25th Judicial District Court, Parish of Plaquemines (Louisiana) granting the exception of no cause of action of defendant, a State of Louisiana employer, inter alia.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the State Department of Wildlife and Fisheries. He was injured while working as a member of the crew of a state owned vessel in navigation and assigned to patrol the waters. The employee filed a petition for damages against his employer, the State, and a co-employee. seeking relief under the Jones Act and general maritime law for his injuries. The State admitted that it was the employer of the employee and the co-employee. The employee argued that the trial court erred in finding that a Louisiana state employee has no rights under the Jones Act or general maritime law to sue his employer, and that workers' compensation was the exclusive remedy. The court agreed. Also, the State had waived its sovereign immunity. under La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A). While the State could restrict Jones Act suits against it by its employees, it had not done so. The court overruled Kuebel v. Department of Wildlife and Fisheries, 08-1018 (La. App. 4 Cir. 4/15/09), 14 So. 2d 20, and followed earlier precedents. The court found that the employee stated a cause of action under the Jones Act and general maritime law against his employer, the State of Louisiana.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court.

State v. Fernandez


NO. 2009-KA-1727


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-1727 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/06/10); 50 So. 3d 219; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1359



October 6, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 10, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Fernandez, 61 So. 3d 682, 2011 La. LEXIS 937 (La., Apr. 8, 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Fernandez v. Rogers, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 151250 (E.D. La., Dec. 12, 2011)
Related proceeding at State v. Novel, 103 So. 3d 746, 2012 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 661 (La.App. 4 Cir., Oct. 24, 2012)
Writ dismissed by State ex rel. Fernandez v. State, 210 So. 3d 272, 2017 La. LEXIS 414 (La., Feb. 24, 2017)
Writ dismissed by State ex rel. Fernandez v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1904 (La., Sept. 15, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 480-784, SECTION "I". HONORABLE KAREN K. HERMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting her, on a jury's verdict, of simple robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65, and second degree kidnapping, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1, and sentencing her as a second felony offender to seven years on the robbery conviction and forty years at hard labor without benefits on the kidnapping conviction.


OVERVIEW: First, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, a reasonable juror could readily have concluded that defendant was a principal to the robbery and kidnapping of the victim. Defendant's actions preceding and during the offense pointed directly to her knowing and voluntary participation in both crimes. Although she was not armed and said nothing during the robbery, she was in the immediate proximity of the vehicle when the robbery took place and voiced no concern over her boyfriend's actions. Further, although defendant was out of sight when the victim was tied up and put in the trunk, a reasonable juror could also have concluded that it was defendant who backed the automobile into the driveway from the street, thereby facilitating the kidnapping. Second, defendant failed to demonstrate that she was unable to obtain a fair and impartial jury through the use of careful voir dire examination. Finally, defendant's midrange sentence of forty years without benefit of parole was neither grossly disproportionate to the crime nor a needless imposition of pain and suffering. Likewise, defendant's seven year sentence for simple robbery was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

919 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Russo v. Kraus


NO. 2010-CA-0178, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2010-CA-0179


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0178 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/29/10); 49 So. 3d 941; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1312



September 29, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 2, 2010.
Writ granted by, Reversed by Russo v. Kraus, 2011 La. LEXIS 255 (La., Jan. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 2006-4436 C/W 2006-6107, DIVISION "I-14". Honorable Piper D. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient's family (collectively, the family), appealed from an order of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), granting summary judgment in favor of defendants, the State and a doctor (collectively, the doctors), finding that the three-year prescriptive period established by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was constitutional, thereby dismissing the family's claims with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Over seven years after a doctor examined tissue from a hysterectomy, the patient discovered a malignant lump in her neck. She later died from cervical cancer. Section 9:5628 as written required medical malpractice claims to be filed within three years of the occurrence of the tort, regardless of the date of discovery. The appellate court declined to find that § 9:5628 was unconstitutional as applied to the patient and third parties with diseases with latency periods in excess of three years by violating La. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 22. Instead, it found that a Sibley hearing was warranted for the purpose of placing into evidence the necessary testimony, documents, and other evidence to permit the trial court to determine whether the proper parties plaintiff were before the court, whether a medical insurance crisis existed when § 9:5628 was enacted, and if the patient's disease was one of the 19 diseases with latency periods in excess of three years. Accordingly, the trial court committed reversible error by failing to hold a Sibley hearing before granting the motions for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.


 

920 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


La. in re K.M.


NO. 2010-CA-0649


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0649 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/29/10); 49 So. 3d 460; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1305



September 29, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 2, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUVENILE COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2009-317-01-DQ-E, SECTION "E". Honorable Tracey Flemings-Davillier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A juvenile appealed a judgment of the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Orleans, Louisiana, which adjudicated her delinquent on the charge of illegal carrying of a weapon in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95. She argued that § 14:95 was unconstitutional, that the evidence was insufficient, and that the juvenile court erred in denying her motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A police officer at a high school observed the juvenile and two other young women walk onto the high school's property. They were not wearing school uniforms, as was required of all students. The officer asked the three for identification; the two others produced identification but the juvenile said she did not have any. She opened her purse to show she did not have identification, and the officer looked into her purse and saw a knife. The court held that the motion to suppress was properly denied. The officer had reasonable suspicion that the juvenile was trespassing on school property; then the juvenile voluntarily opened her large purse and revealed a knife in plain view. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to show that the manner in which the juvenile carried the knife in her purse evinced intent to conceal the knife's identity in violation of § 14:95. The court rejected the juvenile's contention that the language in the statute that it must be "probable" that she was going to use the knife as a dangerous weapon allowed proof of intent by a preponderance of evidence. The intent element was required to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The juvenile's adjudication was affirmed.

 

921 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beauchamp


NO. 2010 KA 0451


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 0451 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/10/10); 49 So. 3d 5; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1214



September 10, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 21st Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Livingston, State of Louisiana. District Court No. 23259. The Honorable Ernest G. Drake, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury in the 21st Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Livingston, Louisiana, of distribution of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A(1). He was sentenced to thirty years at hard labor, with the first two years of the sentence without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A drug enforcement agent saw defendant riding a bicycle and held up four fingers, signaling he wanted to buy $ 40 worth of crack cocaine. They met at a bar and defendant placed crack cocaine on the hood of the undercover vehicle. The agent put $ 40 on the ground, as instructed by defendant, and secured the cocaine. Defendant argued that the State failed to prove all of the elements of the offense, alleging that the State's use of a scientific analysis report to establish that the substance distributed was cocaine violated his right to confrontation, U.S. Const. amend. VI. Four months prior to trial, the State filed a notice of intent to introduce a scientific analysis report at trial, attaching a copy of the report to the notice. The report was made in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:499 and indicated that the evidence was determined to contain cocaine. The court held that admission of the scientific analysis report did not violate defendant's confrontation clause rights. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:501 was precisely the kind of "notice-and-demand" statute that the U.S. Supreme Court in Melendez-Diaz recognized as permissible under the Confrontation Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Lawrence


NO. 2009-KA-1637


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-1637 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/25/2010); 47 So. 3d 1003; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1188



August 25, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 28, 2010.
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Lawrence, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 637 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 447-059, SECTION "A". Honorable Laurie A. White, Judge.
State v. Lawrence, 996 So. 2d 1079, 2008 La. LEXIS 2622 (La., 2008)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR RECONSIDERATION OF SENTENCE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his mandatory sentence of life in prison without probation or parole imposed by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1(B) following a less-than-unanimous jury verdict that defendant was guilty of second degree murder of a one-year-old boy.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's argument that the jury should not have been informed about his plea of guilty four years before the death of the one-year-old boy to a charge of cruelty to his seven-month-old daughter. Evidence of defendant's acknowledged prior act of cruelty to his daughter while maintaining that any harm was accidental was admissible for the purpose of demonstrating the absence of accident regarding the boy. Medical testimony that the boy's death was caused by intentional acts of cruelty, defendant's admission of "play-boxing" with the child, his past act of cruel treatment of his own daughter, and the fact that he was the last person to see the boy alive tended to discount any reasonable hypothesis of innocence. Controlling authority provided that the twelve-person jury's verdict did not have to be unanimous, and defendant's conviction thus was affirmed. However, the district court should have considered defendant's claim that his mandatory life sentence was unconstitutionally excessive under the circumstances of his case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded the matter to the district court for an evidentiary hearing on defendant's claim that his mandatory life sentence was excessive.

Douglas v. Children's Hosp.


NO. 2010-CA-0213


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0213 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/19/10); 69 So. 3d 434; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1178



August 19, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Douglas v. Children's Hosp., 51 So. 3d 10, 2010 La. LEXIS 2982 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by Douglas v. Children's Hosp., 51 So. 3d 15, 2010 La. LEXIS 2983 (La., Dec. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 95-1190, DIVISION "E-7". Honorable Madeleine Landrieu, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents, individually and on behalf of their minor child, sought review of the decision of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant State on plaintiffs' constitutional statutory challenge; limited plaintiffs' recovery in the medical-malpractice action to a single cap; dismissed the jury's awards to the parents; and failed to cast defendants, two doctors, for damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' sought review of a finding in favor of defendants in plaintiffs' medical-malpractice action stemming from their daughter's amputation of her leg. The dismissal on the State's motion for summary judgment of plaintiffs' constitutional challenge under the Malpractice Liability for State Services Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 et seq., was proper because the caps were constitutional. Further, the trial court did not err in finding that plaintiffs' recovery was limited to a single medical malpractice cap. The patient suffered one devastating and life-changing injury, the loss of her leg, a loss to which the jury found the negligence of her three surgeons contributed. The suggestion that the statutory cap was to be applied "per plaintiff" rather than "per patient" was rejected. Thus, there was no error in the deletion of the jury's awards of loss of consortium damages to the parents. Because the judgment did not apply the fault apportionment to the award of past medical expenses, which were not covered by the statutory cap, the judgment was amended to conform to the jury's allocation of 60 percent fault to the doctors, the patient's orthopedic surgeons.


OUTCOME: The appellate court amended the judgment to apply the jury's fault apportionment to the award of past medical expenses and affirmed in all other respects.

 

924 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Gunderson v. F.A. Richard & Assocs.


09-1498


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-1498 (La.App. 3 Cir. 08/16/10); 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1170



August 16, 2010, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE FOURTEEN DAY REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2004-002417. HONORABLE ROBERT L. WYATT, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Gunderson v. F.A. Richard & Assocs., 44 So. 3d 779, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 988 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 30, 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action in which plaintiff healthcare providers (providers) claimed that defendant insurers violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2203.1, the insurers appealed a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which granted the providers' motion for partial summary judgment, awarded statutory damages, and denied the insurer's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The providers alleged that the insurers routinely reimbursed them in workers' compensation cases at lower contracted rates, rather than at the higher mandated workers' compensation rates, thereby violating § 40:2203.1 by failing to provide them with prior notice of their intent to reimburse at those rates. The trial court granted the providers' motion for partial summary judgment and awarded statutory damages. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that while the law of another state may have applied to the contract in general, it could not be used to circumvent the notice requirement. There was no error in the trial court's determination that a ten-year prescriptive period applied to the action. The insurer failed to carry its burden of proving that there was any genuine issue of material fact in dispute or that it could present evidence sufficient to rebut the providers' prima facie case. The trial court did not err in designating the damages portion of its judgment as final.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

925 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 45,429-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,429 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/11/10); 46 So. 3d 756; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1140



August 11, 2010, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Jones v. State, 2013 La. LEXIS 2156 (La., Oct. 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 40-970. Honorable Charles Glenn Fallin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana, of second-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 14:30.1. After his motions for new trial and post verdict judgment of acquittal were denied, defendant was sentenced to the mandatory life term at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the evidence supported the conviction. After he received his Miranda warnings, defendant confessed that he shot the victim at close range. Eyewitnesses confirmed that fact. The victim died from the gunshot wounds. Defendant confronted the victim to settle the tensions that were mounting for weeks, while armed with a pistol. Any threatening text messages sent to defendant by the victim did not prove provocation. There were no mitigating factors for manslaughter. A photograph showing a frontal view of the victim and the bullet wounds, and a photograph taken from the victim's back showing bullet wounds were admissible as they were introduced to establish the victim's identity, and the location, severity, and number of wounds, and to corroborate evidence as to the manner of death. A proper foundation under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:450 was laid for the admission of the tape of defendant's confession. The sentence did not shock the sense of justice in light of the crime committed and the likely risk of harm to others who did not get along with defendant. There was no error patent under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 920(2).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Thomas


NO. 2010-KA-0528, CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2010-K-0303, CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2010-KA-0529


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2010-0528 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/15/10); 54 So. 3d 1; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1048



July 15, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 7, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Thomas, 44 So. 3d 702, 2010 La. LEXIS 1912 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by State v. Thomas, 44 So. 3d 702, 2010 La. LEXIS 1917 (La., 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Thomas v. Louisiana, 131 S. Ct. 556, 178 L. Ed. 2d 411, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 8661 (U.S., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 434-092, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.
State v. Patin, 28 So. 3d 261, 2010 La. LEXIS 430 (La., 2010)
State v. Thomas, 34 So. 3d 279, 2010 La. LEXIS 1131 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted two defendants' motions to quash. The first defendant also argued in his writ application that the district court erred in its failure to bring him to trial in excess of eight years, constituting a violation of the time limitations for the commencement of trial.


OVERVIEW: The case arose out of a shooting. The State argued that the district court abused its discretion in holding that the first defendant could go free without having been tried and that the district court abused its discretion in granting the motion to quash filed by the second defendant on constitutional grounds. The first defendant argued in his writ application that the district court erred in its failure to bring him to trial in excess of eight years, thereby constituting a violation of the time limitations for the commencement of trial. The appellate court reversed its prior affirmation of the granting of the motions to quash the indictments and remanded. The appellate court was unable to say that the State was responsible for the delay by taking a codefendant to trial first. While the decision to try the codefendant first initiated the snowballing effect for the delay, and the delay was further precipitated by Hurricane Katrina and its aftermath, there must be some additional showing that the State did more to hinder defendants' trial. To quash the indictment as to the two defendants when the basis was that not only the State was responsible, constituted clear error.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the granting of the motions to quash filed by defendants, remanded the matter to the district court to reinstate the charges of second-degree murder, and ordered the district court to commence the trials of defendants within 45 days. Further, the district court was ordered to court conduct a bond hearing on the amended charge of second-degree murder.

Gunderson v. F.A. Richard & Assocs.


09-1498


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-1498 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/30/10); 44 So. 3d 779; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 988



June 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment denied by, Partial summary judgment granted by Gunderson v. F.A. Richard & Assocs., 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1170 (La.App. 3 Cir., Aug. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2004-002417. HONORABLE ROBERT L. WYATT, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Gunderson v. F.A. Richard & Assocs., 40 So. 3d 418, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 841 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 2, 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action brought under the Preferred Provider Organization Act (PPOA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2201, et seq., by plaintiff healthcare providers, defendant preferred provider organizations (PPOs), appealed a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment to the healthcare providers for the minimum amount of damages mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2203.1(G).


OVERVIEW: The healthcare providers alleged that the PPOs entered into contracts with them that allowed the PPOs' clients to pay a discounted rate for health care services. They alleged that the PPOs routinely reimbursed them in workers' compensation cases at the lower contracted rates, rather than at the higher mandated workers' compensation rates, thereby violating the provisions of § 40:2203.1 by failing to provide them with prior notice of their intent to reimburse at the PPO rates. The healthcare providers filed a summary judgment motion seeking payment of the minimum amount of damages mandated by § 40:2203.1(G) for each violation, which the trial court granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The PPOs failed to show that the trial court was divested of jurisdiction prior to the hearing on the motions for summary judgment by the grant of a motion for appeal of its motion to decertify the class. The choice of law provision found in the contract did not circumvent the state's interest in the notice requirements of the PPOA. the trial court correctly found that the prescriptive period applicable to an action for violation of the notice requirements of § 40:2203.1 was ten years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Jenkins


NO. 2009-KA-1551


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-1551 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/30/10); 45 So. 3d 173; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1020



June 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 2, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 481-748, SECTION "F". Honorable Robin D. Pittman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) for aggravated battery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34 and attempted aggravated assault upon a police officer with a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Regarding attempted aggravated assault upon a police officer with a firearm, defendant was sentenced to the maximum penalty. He was fleeing from the police and assaulted the officer with a firearm and continued to evade authorities to escape apprehension. The court held that a trial court had broad discretion when imposing a sentence. On appellate review, the relevant question was not whether another sentence might have been more appropriate but whether the trial court abused its broad sentencing discretion. An appellate court had to determine whether the trial court adequately complied with the statutory guidelines in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, as well as whether the facts of the case warranted the sentence imposed. Where the statute provided for a mandatory sentence, it was an exercise in futility for the trial court to enumerate its reasons. Where defendant was convicted of two different crimes against two different victims, aggravated battery was plainly a separate crime from the first and defendant failed to establish that the trial court abused its discretion in ordering that he serve his sentences consecutively pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 883.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

State v. Bourg


09-1291


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-1291 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/30/10); 42 So. 3d 1079; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 985



June 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Bourg, 56 So. 3d 990, 2011 La. LEXIS 300 (La., 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Bourg v. State, 2014 La. LEXIS 289 (La., Feb. 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. LANDRY, NO. 07-K-3432-A. HONORABLE JAMES P. DOHERTY, PRESIDING.
State v. Bourg, 6 So. 3d 1075, 2009 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 191 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction on one count of first degree robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.1, and his sentence by the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry, Louisiana, of 15 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's pro se assignment of error that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction. Defendant held what the victim thought was a knife to the victim's throat and then drove away in the victim's car, and a view of that evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution supported the jury's finding that the essential elements of the crime of first degree robbery were proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also rejected defendant's claim in his attorney-filed brief that his sentence was excessive given his upbringing in the foster care system and minimal education and his relative youth, drug addiction, and lack of job skills. The sentence of 15 years was within the 3 to 40 year range of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:46.1(B) and was within the trial court's discretion, considering defendant's extensive criminal history and his use of an actual weapon in the offense, the danger of defendant committing further offenses upon his release, and defendant's failure to attempt to obtain employment prior to the offense. His sentence was less than the penalty imposed in another case with less aggravating circumstances and more mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

931 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


NO. 09-KA-1043


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-1043 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/29/10); 43 So. 3d 261; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 977



June 29, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 13, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 08-709, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE JOAN S. BENGE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile entered a guilty plea to charges of three counts of armed robbery and one count of second degree kidnapping in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:4 and 14:44.1 respectively. Defendant sought review of sentences by the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which imposed four 30-year concurrent sentences as a result of his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant robbed three victims while armed with a firearm in three separate instances. They also committed the second degree kidnapping of the third victim. The court held that the trial court did not err. During the plea colloquy, the trial court informed defendant that it would sentence him to no more than 30 years at hard labor on each count to run concurrently and explained that it would take testimony at the sentencing hearing. The trial court stated that defendant should not count on less than 30 years. Additionally, the guilty plea form stated that defendant was advised that there would be a cap of 30 years on each count. He indicated that he understood by writing his initials next to that statement. Because those sentences were imposed in conformity with the plea agreement which was set forth in the record at the time of the plea, defendant could not seek review of them under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2, even though they involved sentencing caps. The court also held that trial counsel's failure to file a motion to reconsider the sentence would not prejudice defendant by denying him such review. No errors patent required corrective action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentences.

State v. White


NO. 09-KA-1071


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-1071 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/29/10); 44 So. 3d 750; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 973



June 29, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 13, 2010.
Writ granted by State v. White, 58 So. 3d 454, 2011 La. LEXIS 594 (La., 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. White, 68 So. 3d 508, 2011 La. LEXIS 1590 (La., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 08-2390, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED; MATTER REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), convicting him, on a jury's verdict, of fifth offense driving while intoxicated (DWI), in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(A), (E), and sentencing him to 20 years imprisonment at hard labor to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension, and to run concurrently with a sentence in another case.


OVERVIEW: First, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of fifth offense driving while intoxicated. At the time of his arrest, defendant was asleep in his vehicle with the motor running and the vehicle in drive, but the vehicle was not moving. The total circumstances showed sufficient physical handling of the controls of the car by defendant and a rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was operating the vehicle. Next, the trial court did not err in denying his motion to quash the bill of information. Defendant's prior non-jury DWI misdemeanor convictions were properly used as predicates to enhance the felony DWI sentence, although first and second offense DWI offenders did not have a right to a jury trial. Finally, the twenty year sentence imposed by the trial court was constitutionally excessive after considering the nature of the instant crime, the nature and background of defendant, and similar cases where no one was injured and there was no accident as a result of defendant's intoxication. Accordingly, the court reduced the term to ten years without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction. It amended the sentence by reducing the term to ten years imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. It affirmed the sentence as amended. The court remanded the matter and ordered the trial court to correct the commitment to reflect that the sentence was to be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.
