State v. White


NO. 09-KA-1122


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-1122 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/29/10); 44 So. 3d 309; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 974



June 29, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 13, 2010.
Writ denied by State ex rel. White v. State, 2013 La. LEXIS 1583 (La., June 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 08-740, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE EMILE R. ST. PIERRE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana) convicting him of distribution of heroin, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966A, and sentencing him to 20 years. After the denial of his motion to reconsider sentence, the trial court granted his motion for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The failure to file a motion to reconsider sentence or to state the specific grounds on which the motion was based limited defendant to a review of the sentence for constitutional excessiveness only. The U.S. Const. amend. VIII and La. Const. art. I, § 20 prohibited the imposition of excessive punishment. A sentence was considered excessive if it was grossly disproportionate to the offense. At the time of sentencing, the trial court had before it a pre-sentence investigation report. The report showed that defendant was a third felony offender and defendant admitted to being a heroin addict. He only attended treatment once, in compliance with a court order. He did not follow the program. The report indicated that defendant refused to accept responsibility for any of his offenses. The recommendation of the Department of Corrections was that defendant be multiple billed as a third offender, and that he be sentenced to a term of no less than 25 years. Based on defendant's extensive criminal history, his refusal to cooperate with drug treatment, and the seriousness of the offense, there was no abuse of discretion in sentencing defendant to 20 years.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

934 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morgan


NO. 2009-K-1395


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009 1395 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/23/10); 44 So. 3d 292; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 952



June 23, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 2, 2010.
Writ granted by, Affirmed by State v. Morgan, 48 So. 3d 274, 2010 La. LEXIS 2521 (La., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 271-267 C\W 342-539, 359-171, 371-067, 389-832, 458-106, 458-109. Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Morgan, 32 So. 3d 807, 2010 La. LEXIS 986 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, incompetent criminal defendants, sought relief from a decision from the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana) denying their Motion to Release or Remand to the Department of Health and Hospitals pursuant to a recent amendment of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 648(B)(3).


OVERVIEW: Six criminal defendants had been determined to be permanently incompetent to stand trial for the foreseeable future and a danger to themselves or others. All six were committed pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 648(B)(3) prior to its revision in 2008. The amendment required that an incompetent defendant could only be held for a reasonable time; after that, if his competency was not restored, he had to be civilly committed. In their writ application, defendants argued that the 2008 amendment was retroactive. The court held that in absence of contrary legislative expression, substantive laws applied prospectively only. Procedural and interpretative laws applied both prospectively and retroactively, unless there was a legislative expression to the contrary. While there was no legislative expression as to retroactive application, the court held that the amendment created a procedural mechanism to be used if a trial court determined that an incompetent defendant was unlikely in the foreseeable future to be capable of standing trial and found the amendment to be retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and defendants were remanded to the custody of the Department of Health and Hospitals.

Caddo Fedn. of Teachers & Support Pers. v. Caddo Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 45,357-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,357 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/23/10); 41 So. 3d 1259; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 934



June 23, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Caddo Fed'n. of Teachers & Support Pers. v. Caddo Parish Sch. Bd., 2012 La. App. LEXIS 1215 (La.App. 2 Cir., Sept. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 522,475. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, teachers and a teachers' federation, filed an action against defendant school board seeking a declaratory judgment as to whether the teachers were entitled to additional compensation pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:154.2. The federation challenged a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which granted the school board's exception of no right of action and dismissed it as a party.


OVERVIEW: The teachers sought a declaratory judgment as to whether they were entitled to additional compensation after the school board increased the length of their school day. The federal joined the lawsuit as an association representing other teachers employed by the school board. The school board argued that the federation had no real or actual interest in the proceedings. The court of appeal held that the federation had associational standing to bring the action against the school board on behalf of its members. The teachers, as well as other members of the federation, had standing to sue in their own right. The federation's interests were consistent with the suit. The goal of the federation was no different than most unions and other employee organizations, which was to ensure fair and accurate wages for all of its members. The relief the federation and teachers sought was a declaration pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1871 of whether or not the teachers were entitled to additional compensation pursuant to §17:154.2. The relief requested was not specific to any individual party but merely a clarification of rights for all teachers employed by the school board.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Watts


NO. 2009-KA-0912


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-0912 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/16/10); 41 So. 3d 625; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 921



June 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 19, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Watts, 2011 La. LEXIS 416 (La., Jan. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 473-701, SECTION "J". Honorable Darryl A. Derbigny, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), for violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 through failure to register in Louisiana as a sex offender after being convicted of sexual exploitation of a minor in Washington and taking up residence in Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Washington's statute under which he was convicted as a sex offender, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.040, was not equivalent to Louisiana sex offender statutes because the age limit for a juvenile victim under the Washington statute was eighteen while the age limit under the Louisiana statutes was seventeen. The court rejected defendant's argument given common legislative intent in Washington and Louisiana to criminalize exploitation of children. The court observed that despite difficulties that followed a hurricane, persons other than defendant who moved to Louisiana were able to follow requirements for registering as sex offenders. Also, while defendant contended that his efforts to register showed he had no intent not to register and that § 15:542 was unconstitutional for not containing a criminal intent element, the court held that certain conduct was criminal even in the absence of criminal intent and that the statute was constitutional. The court concluded that the trial court erred only in failing to impose a fine on defendant that was mandatory under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542.1.4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated his sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing to include a mandatory fine on defendant.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment of the City Court of Slidell, Juvenile Division, in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana, which adjudicated him a delinquent child upon finding that he committed the delinquent act of aggravated rape, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, and which committed him to the custody of the department of Public Safety and Corrections, Office of Youth Development.

State v. Sanchez


2010 KA 0016


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2010 0016 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/11/10); 39 So. 3d 834; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 894



June 11, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 466319. Honorable William J. Crain, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle without a lawful presence in the United States under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:100.13. He filed a motion to quash the information, which was denied by the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. He entered a guilty plea. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: In addition to sentencing defendant to 30 days, the trial court ordered that he be held under an Immigration and Naturalization Service detainer. Defendant challenged § 14:100.13, arguing that it was federal preempted, it violated equal protection principles, it was void for vagueness, and he was subject to cruel and unusual punishment. The court found that § 14:100.13 was not federally preempted as it was a valid exercise of the state's police power to regulate public roads. Defendant failed to make a prima facie showing of racial discrimination or raise an inference of such discrimination to support a finding that the Equal Protection Clause or the Fourth Amendment had been violated. Section 14: 100.13 was not void for vagueness as the conduct proscribed was unambiguous. Section 14:100.13 imposed no mandatory minimum prison sentence or fine. While the reporting requirement could trigger deportation, the sentencing provision of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:100.11 was not unconstitutionally excessive. The trial court did not err in denying the motion to quash the bill of information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

J-W Power Co. v. State


NUMBER 2009 CA 2330


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 2330 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/11/10); 40 So. 3d 1214; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 903



June 11, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by J-W Power Co. v. State, 48 So. 3d 1099, 2010 La. LEXIS 2369 (La., 2010)
Affirmed by J-W Power Co. v. State through Dep't of Revenue & Taxation, 2011 La. LEXIS 606 (La., Mar. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 530,238. Honorable Timothy Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parent corporation sought a refund of taxes paid to respondent Department of Revenue in the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1576. The trial court granted the Department's exception of no right of action, arguing that the parent was not the taxpayer and was therefore not entitled to seek a refund of tax money. The parent appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parent was a provider of gas compression services. Two of its customers were two wholly-owned subsidiaries. These subsidiaries were required to pay sales tax on full service agreement contracts. The parent, as the selling dealer, was required to collect the new sales tax from its customers and remit those taxes to the Department. The Department argued that because the parent was not itself the taxpayer, it did not have the right to seek a refund. The parent then alleged that it was the agent of the two subsidiaries and was bringing its action on their behalf pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 694. The Department argued that the subsidiaries, the actual taxpayers, did not personally protest the tax payments as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1576. The court held that the parent satisfied the prerequisites of § 47:1576, inasmuch as the payments were made, notice was given to the Department that the payments were protested, and the suit against the proper party was timely filed. It was not required to disclose its agency relationship in its protest letters; however, the letters clearly indicated that the parent was not itself the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter to the district court for further proceedings.

Toups v. City of Shreveport


No. 44,933-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,933 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/02/10); 37 So. 3d 406; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 819



June 2, 2010, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Toups v. City of Shreveport, 50 So. 3d 822, 2010 La. LEXIS 2528 (La., 2010)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by Toups v. City of Shreveport, 2011 La. LEXIS 609 (La., Mar. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Rehearing Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 517,677. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.
Toups v. City of Shreveport, 37 So. 3d 406, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 169 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought judicial review in the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), of the decision of appellee city council reversing the decision of a zoning board of appeals (ZBA) granting the retailer a special exception for a liquor store. The owner appealed, the trial court affirmed the council's decision, and the appellate court granted rehearing to further review whether the council abused its discretion.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held the city council acted arbitrarily and capriciously because (1) the owner met ZBA requirements, addressing concerns of those opposed to the use, (2) it was not alleged that the owner's application was not properly investigated, (3) the property was commercially zoned, (4) the store met a requirement to be more than 300 feet from schools, churches or synagogues, and playgrounds, (5) no substantial relationship to the public health, safety, morals or general welfare justifying denial was shown, as no objective facts supported claims that the store would cause heavier traffic, drunk drivers, and a higher violent crime rate, (6) neither the council nor the trial court were given "two opinions" but were presented with the opposition's opinion versus rational and objective facts supporting the application, and (7) the council did more than necessary to regulate the business of selling alcohol, given the objective evidence before it, contrary to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

State v. Lewis


NO. 09-KA-783


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-783 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/28/10); 43 So. 3d 973; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 812



May 28, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 13, 2010.
Rehearing denied by State v. Lewis, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1064 (La.App. 5 Cir., July 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-3958, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE ELLEN S. KOVACH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), convicting him, upon a jury's verdict, of terrorizing, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:40.1, and sentencing him to serve 12 years in the custody of the Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made calls to a corporation's customer service department and spoke to representatives in Mexico and Florida. He became very angry and threatened to blow up a repair facility in Texas. The evidence was sufficient to show that defendant intentionally communicated information to representatives that the commission of a violent crime was imminent, or that a circumstance dangerous to human life was about to exist. Further, the evidence was sufficient to find that defendant had the specific intent to cause members of the general public to be in sustained fear for their safety. The customer service agent felt fear, alarm, or agitation of danger. She immediately contacted her supervisor, who alerted other personnel of the threats. Also, the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant had the specific intent to cause the evacuation of a building and a serious disruption to the general public. Next, defendant's sentence was less than the maximum and no fine was imposed. Further, defendant had an extensive criminal history. Therefore, defendant's sentence was not constitutionally excessive. Finally, there was no merit to defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Fields v. Walpole Tire Serv., L.L.C.


NO. 45,206-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,206 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/19/10); 37 So. 3d 549; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 726



May 19, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Fields v. Walpole Tire Serv., L.L.C., 2010 La. LEXIS 2091 (La., Oct. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 511022. Honorable Eugene W. Bryson, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff truck driver brought a products liability action under the Louisiana Products Liability Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.51 et seq., against defendants, a manufacturer and a tire service company. The driver's employer and its compensation insurer intervened. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) entered judgment on a jury's verdict in favor of the manufacturer. The driver and the intervenors appealed.


OVERVIEW: Approximately two weeks after a tire was retreaded, a zipper rupture occurred in the tire. The pressure from the rupture knocked the truck driver to the ground, causing him to sustain serious injuries. The jury was not manifestly erroneous in concluding that the tire did not contain a defect that rendered it unreasonably dangerous in construction or composition, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.55, where defense experts opined that the rupture was caused by under-inflation. The jury was entitled to credit the defense experts' opinions over the truck driver's evidence. Further, the manufacturer's motion for directed verdict was properly granted with regard to the manufacturer's alleged failure to conform to an express warranty, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.58, because there were no promises or guarantees contained in the data sheet with regard to the life of a retreaded tire. Additionally, the manufacturer's motion for directed verdict was properly granted with regard to the manufacturer's alleged failure to warn, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.57(A), because there was no admissible evidence concerning the manufacturer's failure to warn consumers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Barlow v. Town of Waterproof


No. 45,211-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,211 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/19/10); 39 So. 3d 768; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 725



May 19, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Tensas, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 22,635. Honorable Michael E. Lancaster, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town clerk filed suit against defendant town mayor in the Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Tensas, Louisiana, seeking to prohibit the mayor from interfering with the clerk's job duties and compensation. The trial court issued a preliminary injunction forbidding the mayor from taking any action that would upset the status quo of the clerk's job duties and employment. The mayor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The clerk alleged that disagreements arose between her, the mayor, and the police chief over the processing of speeding tickets and the withholding of out-of-state drivers' licenses from ticketed drivers. The mayor reduced her duties and pay and minimized her authority. The court held that the appeal was timely under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 3612(C) and 2087 because the filing of the signed judgment into the suit record occurred within 15 days of the mayor's motion for appeal. The mayor argued that the injunction impinged upon his statutory duty to supervise the town clerk under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:404. The court concluded that the mayor's actions extended well beyond his general powers of supervision and direction of the administration of the municipality's affairs, so that the clerk's defined duties owed to the municipality (such as those under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 33:422, 33:381, 33:406, and 33:421) were violated. The balance between the mayoral power and the clerk's duties was required to be kept unless the mayor and aldermen agreed to the clerk's removal as required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 33:386(A) and 33:404(A)(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of a preliminary injunction.

946 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Burch v. Hancock Holding Co.


NUMBER 2009 CA 1839


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 1839 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/07/10); 39 So. 3d 742; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 670



May 7, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from Twenty-Second Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Washington, State of Louisiana. Docket Number 96553. Honorable Raymond S. Childress, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, including the daughter, the estate and the grandchildren of a tort victim, filed a petition for wrongful death and survival action damages. The estate and the grandchildren appealed a judgment of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Washington, Louisiana, sustaining exceptions of defendants, a bank and an insurer, based on the objections of no right and no cause of action.


OVERVIEW: A tort victim died after tripping over uneven flooring at branch of the bank. The court affirmed dismissal of claims of the grandchildren and the estate because Louisiana's survival and wrongful death causes of action, found in La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.1 and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.2, provided rights only to specified survivors that included the surviving spouse, children, parents, grandparents, and siblings of the deceased. Rights provided by survival and wrongful death causes of action thus passed only to survivors of the tort victim in the statutory order of exclusionary preference and not in an inheritance sense or through the victim's succession. The court also held that the statutes did not violate equal protection rights under La. Const. art. I, § 3. The legislature had to place some limit on the statutory causes of action, and persons in addition to grandchildren who lived with or were supported by tort victims, such as foster children or unmarried partners, were similarly excluded. The legislature chose to provide relief to those most affected by the death of a tort victim while providing a reasonably appropriate limitation on such rights of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the claims of the estate and the grandchildren.

Rodriguez v. Integrity Contr.


09-1537 consolidated with 09-1538 and 09-1539


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Garcia v. State, 38 So. 3d 526, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 619 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2010)
Writ denied by Rodriguez v. Integrity Contr., 45 So. 3d 1074, 2010 La. LEXIS 2144 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by Rodriguez v. Integrity Contr., 45 So. 3d 1076, 2010 La. LEXIS 2138 (La., 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Vaughan Roofing & Sheet Metal, LLC v. Garcia Rodriguez, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1851 (U.S., Feb. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION # 4, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 04-1827. SHARON MORROW, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. ADDITIONAL ATTORNEY FEES AWARDED FOR WORK PERFORMED ON APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee claimant sought compensation benefits from appellants, his direct employer, its insurer, and a statutory employer, who demanded indemnification from the insurer. The Office of Workers' Compensation, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), found the employers and the insurer jointly liable for benefits, penalties, and attorney fees. It ordered indemnification under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1063. The statutory employer and the insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured when he fell from a roof while performing roofing work for his direct employer. The insurer denied coverage, asserting that the direct employer failed to pay its premium. The claimant alleged that the statutory employer had a contract for repair work and that the direct employer was performing as a subcontractor. The statutory employer denied that relationship, and asserted that the claimant was not liable for benefits because he was an undocumented worker, having remained in the country after the expiration of a work visa. However, the claimant was a statutory employee under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1061, and the statutory employer failed to meet its burden of showing the application of some specific exclusion under which benefits could have been denied. Further, the workers' compensation judge correctly determined that the Office of Workers' Compensation lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the contractual indemnification claim, and properly granted the statutory indemnification claim pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1063. Finally, the record supported the determination that the insurer failed to prove the effective termination of the policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, and awarded additional attorney fees for the appeal.

 

948 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Olde Nawlins Cookery, L.L.C. v. Edwards


2009 CA 1189


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 1189 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/03/10); 38 So. 3d 1012; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 601



May 3, 2010, Date of Judgment


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NUMBER 2008-0003400, PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an alcoholic beverage permit applicant, sought a writ of mandamus against defendants sheriff and parish council seeking issuance of a permit, as well as declaratory relief that a parish ordinance was unconstitutional. The 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana, denied both the requested writ of mandamus and declaratory relief. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Although the district court denied the alternative writ of mandamus and declaratory relief on February 27, 2009, the applicant did not file its appeal until March 23, 2009, well after the ten-day period necessary to perfect its appeal as provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:106B and 303B. Therefore, the court refused to consider that portion of the judgment denying the alternative writ of mandamus, which was actually a request for a review of the withholding of the retail alcoholic beverage permit. The applicant contended that an ordinance requiring written consent of adjacent property owners before an alcoholic beverage permit could be issued in a residential area was unlawful and unconstitutional. The parties stipulated that the applicant's premises were located in a mixed-use area, conceding that the area included some residential use. The parish council's construction of the ordinance to include the mixed-use area as a residential area was a common sense one that was reasonable. The council had authority to enact the ordinance from the provisions of its Home Rule Charter, pursuant to La. Const. Art. VI, § 5.


OUTCOME: The court refused to review the portion of the judgment denying the writ of mandamus. The court affirmed the denial of the applicant's request for declaratory relief.

 

949 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Herndon


No. 45,146-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,146 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/28/10); 36 So. 3d 434; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 591



April 28, 2010, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Succession of Herndon, 2010 La. LEXIS 2070 (La., Sept. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 257,292. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an intestate decedent's illegitimate children, filed a petition in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, seeking to annul and vacate a judgment of possession of the decedent's estate in favor of defendants, the decedent's siblings. The siblings filed a peremptory exception of prescription, which the trial court granted. The children appealed.


OVERVIEW: The children were born to the decedent and their mother during an 11-year-period, 1950 to 1961, in which decedent and the mother resided together unmarried. The decedent died intestate in 1977, never having formally acknowledged the children. In 1977, children born outside of marriage could not inherit from the intestate estate of an alleged father if there was a legitimate relative, and the siblings received the decedent's estate. Then, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 208 and 209 were revised to allow such children to inherit. Unacknowledged or informally acknowledged children born outside of marriage who had already attained the age of 19, or whose alleged parent was already deceased, could bring a civil proceeding to prove their filiation, but such an action had to be brought prior to September 12, 1982, which the children did not do. They argued that they should be allowed to prove paternity by showing that the mother lived in a state of concubinage with the father when the child was conceived. The court held that such evidence was relevant, but would have had to have been presented during a civil proceeding brought during the grace period accorded to the children by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting the siblings' peremptory exception of prescription.

State v. Aguilar


NO. 09-KA-927


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-927 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/13/10); 39 So. 3d 719; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 521



April 13, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 14, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Aguilar, 2010 La. LEXIS 2857 (La., Dec. 10, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 08-4726, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a judge in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, of simple robbery, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65. The trial judge sentenced defendant to seven years' imprisonment at hard labor, with credit for time served. On appeal, he argued that he received an excessive sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, age 23, admitted that he and two friends saw the victim, an elderly gentleman who owned a bar, leave a bank with a bag that they guessed contained money. They followed him in their car, and when he exited his car, defendant jumped on him, knocked him to the ground, and wrestled the bag from him. When a witness tried to intervene, one of the friends got out of the car and threatened him with a knife. The court held that the sentence was not constitutionally excessive. In factually similar cases, other courts had held that the imposition of the maximum sentence for simple robbery was not constitutionally excessive. Defendant acted without provocation and, in committing the robbery, knocked the elderly victim to the ground, causing minor physical injuries. The co-defendant's approach with a knife created a risk of death or great bodily harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence but remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to inform defendant of the prescriptive period for seeking post-conviction relief in writing and to correct the commitment to reflect that (1) defendant was not informed of the prescriptive period for seeking post-conviction relief, and that (2) the original charge against defendant was not amended.

State v. Broussard


09-1012


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-1012 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/07/10); 33 So. 3d 1036; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 507



April 7, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 121791. HONORABLE PATRICK MICHOT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED, RENDERED, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which convicted him of second-degree battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for second-degree battery and the appellate court overturned the conviction, rendered judgment finding him guilty of simple battery, and remanded for resentencing. There was no testimony that the victim lost consciousness and no evidence of disfigurement or permanent disability; protracted loss or impairment of the function of a member, organ, or mental faculty; or a substantial risk of death. Therefore, the State was required to prove that the victim suffered extreme physical pain. But, the victim was not asked about her injuries and, although she sought medical treatment, no medical evidence was submitted. Thus, the State failed to prove that the victim suffered extreme physical. However, a conviction for simple battery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:35 was proper because no evidence even remotely suggested that the victim consented to the attack.


OUTCOME: The appellate court overturned the conviction, rendered judgment finding defendant guilty of simple battery, and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Archield


09-1116


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-1116 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/07/10); 34 So. 3d 434; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 504



April 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Archield v. State, 63 So. 3d 972, 2011 La. LEXIS 1323 (La., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Archield v. State, 133 So. 3d 676, 2014 La. LEXIS 535 (La., 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Archield v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125283 (W.D. La., Aug. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR598-08. HONORABLE C. KERRY ANDERSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE FOR AGGRAVATED BURGLARY AFFIRMED. SENTENCE FOR AGGRAVATED RAPE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED. REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Thirty Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana), convicting him of aggravated burglary, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60, and aggravated rape, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62, and sentencing him to life imprisonment without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence for the rape and 30 years imprisonment at hard labor for the burglary.


OVERVIEW: First, there was no double jeopardy because the crimes of aggravated rape and aggravated battery were separate and distinct offenses. Further, separate and distinct evidence was presented for both crimes. Defendant could have been convicted of aggravated burglary without proof that any rape occurred, considering that he committed battery upon the victim after he forcibly gained entrance into the house. Second, the trial court considered appropriate factors and particularized its reasons for imposing consecutive sentences. It was persuaded to impose consecutive sentences in light of defendant's extensive criminal history, persistence in committing sex offenses, and ineffectiveness of previous leniency by the courts in persuading defendant to cease his criminal behavior. Third, because life imprisonment was not a sentence for a stated number of years or months, the trial court lacked authority to deny eligibility for diminution of the aggravated rape sentence pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 890.1. Finally, the record supported the trial court's determination that the probative nature of other crimes evidence substantially outweighed any risk of unfair prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and the sentence for aggravated burglary. It amended the aggravated rape sentence by deleting the portion denying diminution of sentence, and it affirmed the sentence as amended. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for the limited purpose of noting the amendment to defendant's sentence for aggravated rape in the minutes.

Jones v. City of Pineville


09-1227


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-1227 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/07/10); 34 So. 3d 452; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 487



April 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Jones v. City of Pineville, 2010 La. LEXIS 2529 (La., Nov. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 220,225. HONORABLE MARY LAUVE DOGGETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firefighter sought review of the decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which found in favor of defendant municipality and upheld the civil service board's (board) termination of the firefighter for insubordination.


OVERVIEW: After he failed to give a valid urine sample at the designated facility for a drug screen after having been ordered to do so, the municipality terminated the firefighter for insubordination. The board upheld his termination and the district court affirmed the board's decision. The appellate court reversed, however, stating that the firefighter's termination was not in good faith and was unreasonable because the municipality failed to prove that it performed its affirmative duty to give the firefighter written notice of his termination and the reasons for that termination as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2500(D). The appellate court ordered that the firefighter be reinstated to his former position and that he be paid back pay from the time of his illegal termination. The board's record contained no evidence that the municipality complied with its affirmative duty as delineated in § 33:2500(D). As such, the municipality was in legal bad faith when the firefighter did not receive a written statement of his termination and reasons therefor, and the board's affirmation of the termination without the required written statement was unreasonable, as their decision had no basis.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the district court's affirmation of the board's decision and ordered that the firefighter be reinstated to his former position and that he be paid back pay from the time of his illegal termination. All costs of the appeal were assessed to the city.

State v. Lewis


09-846


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-846 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/07/10); 33 So. 3d 1046; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 512



April 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Lewis, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 749 (La.App. 3 Cir., May 19, 2010)
Writ denied by State v. Lewis, 50 So. 3d 825, 2010 La. LEXIS 2788 (La., 2010)
Later proceeding at State v. Lewis, 118 So. 3d 116, 2013 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 481 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lewis v. Cain, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 113228 (W.D. La., Mar. 24, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERNON, NO. 67408. HONORABLE JAMES RICHARD MITCHELL, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), defendant was found guilty on two counts of first degree murder, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence on each count, to run consecutively. A motion for appeal was iled and granted. Defendant asserted numerous assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: The assignments of error failed. Defendant was not faced with the prospect of the death penalty, nor was he prejudiced by not being afforded a jury trial. Conversely, it was by his request that he was given a bench trial. The trial court heard a codefendant's testimony and defendant's argument that the codefendant committed the offenses. The trial court chose to believe defendant committed the offenses. Defendant used deadly force against an unarmed victim who had his face and arm reconstructed and whose arm was in a cast. Thus, the trial court could rationally have concluded that defendant did not act in self-defense, that his actions were not justified, and his response was excessive. The warrant at issue was signed at 9:49 p.m. and executed that night. Further, at trial, a detective testified that it was not clear whether he could search defendant's residence at night. Based on this information, the police were acting in good faith when they executed the search warrant at night. Although defendant alleged he was denied adequate development of his defense, he failed to prove that his defense was actually altered or that he was denied any funding that was requested.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for first degree murder were affirmed.

State v. Martin


2009 CA 1417


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 1417 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/30/10); 37 So. 3d 1021; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 443



March 30, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 2009 10697, Division "C". Honorable Richard A. Swartz, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State filed a petition for forfeiture under the Seizure and Controlled Dangerous Substances Property Forfeiture Act of 1989, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:2601-40:2622, and an exception of no cause of action, alleging that defendant driver's claim that his property was not subject to forfeiture was untimely. The driver challenged an order of the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, which dismissed his claim.


OVERVIEW: A state police trooper pulled over the driver's vehicle for improper lane usage, searched the vehicle, and found $ 46,750. The driver could not satisfactorily explain the origin of the money, and it was seized pending forfeiture. The court of appeal held that there was no defect in the service of the notice of pending forfeiture on the driver. The Act allowed personal service of the notice, and the driver was personally served by the designated law enforcement agent in accord with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:2607(B)(2) and 2608(3)(a). The trial court erred in sustaining the State's exception of no cause of action. The driver's claim clearly stated a cause of action for the return of the money. However, his claim that his property was not subject to seizure and forfeiture was untimely, rendering it invalid under the Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2610. The State demonstrated by some credible evidence that the money was probably drug related. The money had the distinct odor of marijuana, and the driver could not explain its origin. Therefore, the State satisfied its burden of establishing probable cause for the forfeiture of the funds under the Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2615(A).


OUTCOME: The court of appeal affirmed the judgment dismissing the driver's claim and ordering forfeiture of the money.

Police Jury Ass'n of La. v. State


NO. 2009 CA 1438


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 1438 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/26/10); 36 So. 3d 942; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 457



March 26, 2010, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 569,748. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, non-profit corporations, filed suit against defendants State and governor in the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, seeking to have the Consumer Choice for Television Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 45:1361-1378, declared unconstitutional. Two cable companies intervened on the side of defendants. The district court declared the Act constitutional, and the corporations appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 45:1365B, incumbent service providers had the option to terminate existing cable or video service franchises issued by local governmental subdivisions. The corporations argued that § 45:1365B violated La. Const. art. VII, § 15, by releasing incumbent service providers from obligations owed to local governmental subdivisions under existing franchise agreements. Art. VII, § 15, provided that the legislature could not release, extinguish, or authorize the releasing or extinguishing of any indebtedness, liability, or obligation to the state, a parish, or a municipality. The court held that art. VII, § 15 did not deny the legislature the power to release future obligations owed to municipalities such as local governments affected by the Act. The constitutional issue would arise only if a statute released obligations due and owing prior to the enactment of the statute. The legislature specifically considered and clearly provided that the Act was not intended to release existing obligations at the time that an incumbent service provider exercised its opt-in rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Lomax


NO. 2009-KA-1129

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of possession of heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(C)(1) and sentencing him to ten years at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was also charged with being a felon in possession of a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1. He filed a motion to sever the counts, arguing that if the counts were tried together, the jury would have been unduly influenced by the State suggesting that he was a dangerous man in possession of a firearm. However, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying the motion because defendant failed to show that the jurors would have been confused by the presentation of the evidence, that they could not have segregated evidence as to the two counts, or that he was prejudiced by the joinder of offenses. Proof of the prior specifically enumerated felony conviction was an essential element pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, and the State was entitled to produce evidence of the name and nature of the prior conviction. Finally, La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782(A) were not unconstitutional and, hence, not violative of defendant's U.S. Const. amend. VI right to trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Roche


NO. 09-KA-684


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-684 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/23/10); 39 So. 3d 706; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 402



March 23, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 14, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Roche, 49 So. 3d 396, 2010 La. LEXIS 2739 (La., 2010)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Roche v. State, 2013 La. LEXIS 141 (La., Jan. 18, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-6392, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, which sentenced him to 30-years for distribution of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his 30-year sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. Defendant maintained that the trial court improperly imposed a maximum sentence on the basis he failed to appear for sentencing. Defendant contended he was not the worst offender and, therefore, a maximum sentence was not warranted. The State contended that defendant was precluded from raising the excessiveness of his sentence because it was imposed pursuant to a plea agreement. The instant court found that defendant was precluded from challenging the excessiveness of his sentence on appeal because his sentence was imposed in conformity with a plea agreement that was set forth in the record at the time of the plea. The trial court warned defendant in open court that if he failed to appear he would not receive the 10-year sentence with a boot camp recommendation, but rather he would face a possible maximum sentence. Defendant failed to appear for sentencing, and as a result, he received the maximum 30-year sentence. Defendant was clearly informed of the two possible sentences, which were dictated by his actions, when he entered his plea.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. George


NO. 2008-KA-1193 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-KA-1338 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2009-KA-0561 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2009-KA-0630 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2009-KA-0867


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1193 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/10/10); 34 So. 3d 941; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 330



March 10, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 13, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. George, 50 So. 3d 813, 2010 La. LEXIS 2575 (La., 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by George v. Louisiana, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 3764 (U.S., May 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEALS FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 476-787 C/W 476-116 C/W 480-666 SECTION "A". Honorable Laurie A. White, Judge CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 481-174 SECTION "J". Honorable Darryl A. Derbigny, Judge CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 482-849 SECTION "I". Honorable Karen K. Herman, Judge.
State v. George, 27 So. 3d 289, 2010 La. LEXIS 304 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, each defendant was charged with violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E), second or third offense possession of marijuana. Each defendant sought review of the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana)'s denial of a motion to quash the charge based on a claim that the enhancement of the charge was unconstitutional because it used at least one prior misdemeanor conviction for which a jury trial was not available.


OVERVIEW: Although the trial court in each case rejected the argument, a different section of criminal district court found that the argument had merit and held that § 40:966(E) was unconstitutional. The supreme court subsequently reversed that ruling, denied certification, and remanded the cases for consideration. It held that § 40:966(E)(2) did not suffer from a constitutional infirmity. U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV did not preclude the sentence-enhancing use of a prior valid, fair, and reliable adult misdemeanor conviction, where the misdemeanor proceeding included all the applicable constitutional protections, even though those protections did not include the right to trial by jury. Reliability was the sine qua non for use of prior convictions to enhance a sentence under the prior conviction exception, and not the right to a jury trial. Louisiana's statutory scheme satisfied the requirement of due process because under the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments, states were allowed the presumption that in petty crimes and offenses, trial judges were capable of reliable fact finding. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in denying defendants' motions to quash.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences.

State v. England

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT

ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-4417, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED; MOTION TO WITHDRAW GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for second degree murder. After defendant's motion to suppress statement was denied, the indictment was amended to charge him with manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31. Defendant pleaded guilty to manslaughter and, pursuant to a plea agreement, was sentenced to 40 years with the Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed. His counsel filed a motion to withdraw.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel wrote a brief stating that there were no non-frivolous issues for appeal. The court considered the whole record. It found that the indictment plainly, concisely, and definitely stated the essential facts constituting the offense charged. It also sufficiently identified defendant and the crime charged, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 464-66. The record showed that defendant was aware he was pleading guilty to manslaughter. He was advised of his right to a jury trial, his right to confrontation, and his privilege against self-incrimination, and he waived those rights. Defendant indicated that he was satisfied with the representation of his attorney. He stated that he had not been forced, coerced, or threatened to enter his guilty plea. Defendant was advised that he faced a possible sentencing range of up to 40 years imprisonment at hard labor, and was told that the sentence he would receive would be 40 years imprisonment at hard labor. His sentence fell within the sentencing range prescribed by statute and was imposed pursuant to a plea agreement. The court found that remand was necessary for correction of the commitment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence and granted appellate counsel's motion to withdraw as attorney of record.

State v. Phillips


NO. 09-KA-455


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-455 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/09/10); 39 So. 3d 610; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 318



March 9, 2010, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-2019, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), convicting him of aggravated incest in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1, sentencing him to 15 years at hard labor, and imposing a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for specific performance of an alleged plea bargain. He claimed there was an agreement between himself, his counsel, the prosecutor and the trial judge, that he would receive a five-year probated sentence in exchange for his guilty plea. The trial court denied the motion stating that the waiver of rights form indicated that the sentence would be determined and there was no mention of probation or any determined sentence. Additionally, defendant did not object to his sentence at the time it was imposed. Defendant failed to carry his burden of showing there was an agreement between him and the State regarding a probated sentence and, thus, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for specific performance of a plea bargain. Defendant next claimed that his sentence was constitutionally excessive. Considering the jurisprudence and the circumstances of the case, including the repeated incidents of the crime upon defendant's step-daughter over a three-year period and defendant's lack of remorse, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by imposing the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. It affirmed in part defenant's sentence, but vacated it as to the imposition of the sex offender treatment program. The court remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to correct the commitment to reflect the imposition of a fine on defendant and to transmit the amended minute entry to the officer in charge of the institution to which defendant had been sentenced.

State v. Woods


NO. 09-KA-399


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-399 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/09/10); 38 So. 3d 391; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 319



March 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 14, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Woods, 2010 La. LEXIS 2437 (La., Oct. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-4163, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE DONALD A. ROWAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), finding him to be a fourth felony offender and sentencing him to life imprisonment in his habitual offender proceeding pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially convicted of attempted simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling, possession of hydrocodone, and possession of alprazolam. After defendant's convictions were affirmed on appeal, the State filed the habitual offender bill. The State sought to enhance defendant's sentence by producing evidence of seven prior convictions in which defendant pleaded guilty. The State proved defendant's identity in all of the predicate convictions, the existence of the predicate guilty pleas, and that defendant was represented by counsel. Defendant failed to meet his burden of producing some affirmative evidence of an infringement of his rights or of a procedural irregularity. The State showed that defendant was personally advised of his Boykin rights by the trial judge, and that he waived those rights. Boykin did not require the trial judge to advise defendant of the minimum and maximum sentence, or the possibility of the filing of a future habitual offender bill. While defendant received a double enhancement based on prior convictions for marijuana distribution and possession of a firearm as a felon, the State proved his status independent of either of those convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Lawrence


No. 45,061-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,061 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/03/10); 32 So. 3d 329; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 278



March 3, 2010, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Lawrence, 46 So. 3d 1265, 2010 La. LEXIS 2298 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lawrence v. Warden, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 131869 (W.D. La., July 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 41-244. Honorable Glenn Fallin, Judge.
State v. Stowe, 25 So. 3d 945, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1787 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana, of possession of over 400 grams of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(c). He was sentenced to 30 years' imprisonment without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car that was stopped for weaving. The driver and passenger gave inconsistent stories as to where they had been, and defendant acted nervous and told the officer that he was calling his "legal people." The officer conducted a K-9 search of the vehicle; the search yielded nine pounds of cocaine. Defendant's fingerprint was found on one of the bags. Defendant argued that, because he was only a passenger and did not have any cocaine on his person, the single fingerprint was insufficient to support his conviction. The court held that the evidence, including evidence that defendant had driven the car and admitted loading the items in the trunk, was sufficient. The court held that the officers had grounds for a lawful traffic stop during which they were permitted to check the licenses of both the driver and passenger and call for the K-9 search. Although the admission of audio of the officers conducting a background check on defendant was error, the error was harmless. The trial judge erred in ordering that the entire 30-year sentence be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(G).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but reversed the sentence and remanded for resentencing.

Estopinal v. Parish of St. Bernard


NO. 2009-CA-1382


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-1382 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/24/10); 32 So. 3d 991; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 259



February 24, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 22, 2010.
Application denied by Estopinal v. Parish of St. Bernard, 28 So. 3d 275, 2010 La. LEXIS 437 (La., 2010)
Decision reached on appeal by Estopinal v. Parish of St. Bernard, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 2708 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 5, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM ST. BERNARD 34TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, NO. 113-313, DIVISION "C". Hon. Robert J. Klees, Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, insured homeowners, filed suit against defendant insurer in the St. Bernard 34th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), alleging that their house was wrongfully demolished pursuant to an ordinance governing the Housing Code for the Parish of St. Bernard. The insurer filed an exception of no cause of action, which was granted. The insureds appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insureds alleged that the demolition of their home was a loss that was covered by their "all risk" policy of hazard insurance provided by the insurer. The insurer argued that the policy issued by it contained an exclusion, which precluded coverage for losses caused directly or indirectly by enforcement of a law or ordinance regulating the demolition of property. The policy excluded losses caused by "enforcement of any ordinance or law regulating the use, construction, repair, or demolition of a building or other structure." The court held that this language was not ambiguous and therefore was not subject to interpretation. The exclusion precluded coverage for losses caused directly or indirectly by enforcement of a law or ordinance regulating the demolition of property. The trial court correctly granted the insurer's exception of no cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the exception of no cause of action.


 

966 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Apasra Props., LLC v. City of New Orleans


NO. 2009-CA-0709


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-0709 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/11/10); 31 So. 3d 615; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 207



February 11, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2009-753, DIVISION "J-13". Honorable Nadine M. Ramsey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which denied their request for a writ of preliminary injunction enjoining administrative proceedings brought against them by defendants, a city and a commission. They argued that New Orleans, La., Mun. Code § 6-31 et seq., was unconstitutional, and the enforcement of city code violations rested exclusively with the city's municipal court.


OVERVIEW: The commission cited the owners' properties for violations of historic district ordinances. The court of appeal held that 1921 La. Const. art. XIV, § 22(A) provided the authority for the city to create the Administrative Adjudication Bureau for Public Health, Housing and Environmental Violations, Department of Health (AAB) to adjudicate violations of its ordinances. La. Const. art. VI, § 17 retained that authority for the commission. The creation of the AAB did not violate the city's home rule charter. The Louisiana Constitution, which retained the authority for the commission, and La. Rev. Stat. § 13:2575 empowered the city to enact ordinances and to exercise state police power in order to regulate the use of property situated within the commission for the purpose of historic preservation. The AAB did not have authority pursuant to § 6-31 et seq. to adjudicate the violations alleged against the owners. The alleged violations did not fall within the purview of "housing violations" since they did not constitute a threat to the public health, safety, and welfare and/or to the environment. Jurisdiction for prosecuting the alleged violations existed only in the city's municipal court.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings, and upon remand, the owners were granted leave to amend their petition to seek appropriate relief. It affirmed the trial court's decision to deny the writ of preliminary injunction.

State v. Jones


NO. 09-KA-688


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-688 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/09/10); 33 So. 3d 306; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 200



February 9, 2010, Decided

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Jones v. Warden, Wash. Corr. Ctr. Franklinton, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 161109 (E.D. La., Sept. 13, 2012)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Jones v. State, 138 So. 3d 619, 2014 La. LEXIS 953 (La., Apr. 17, 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Jones v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1940 (La., Sept. 15, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-4622, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions entered by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) for felon in possession of a firearm, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1; possession with intent to distribute marijuana, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A); possession of cocaine between 28 and 199 grams, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F); and possession of a firearm with an obliterated serial number, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1788.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's arguments failed. Defendant argued the evidence was insufficient. He contended the State failed to prove he was in either actual or constructive possession of the drugs and the firearms; however, a loaded firearm was found under the hood of the car he was driving, the vehicle was registered to a family member of defendant, and the evidence showed it was not the first time defendant drove the car. Defendant fled from the police when they approached to investigate what they believed to be a drug transaction and defendant discarded bags of marijuana and crack cocaine, packaged for distribution, while fleeing from the police. Additionally, items used in the packaging of drugs for distribution were found in the apartment where defendant's personal belongings were found. The photographic identification, even if suggestive, was reliable as there was no substantial likelihood of misidentification. Only minutes passed from the sergeant's encounter with the suspect and his identification of defendant from the photograph, and the sergeant's description matched defendant. The ineffective assistance claims were without merit.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Turner


No. 44,920-KA, No. 44, 921-KA (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,920 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/03/10); 32 So. 3d 277; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 128



February 3, 2010, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Turner v. State, 2011 La. LEXIS 749 (La., Mar. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of West Carroll, Louisiana. Trial Court No. F2007060 and F2009017. Honorable Terry A. Doughty, Judge.
State v. Jones, 4 So. 3d 950, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 288 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of West Carroll (Louisiana), which convicted him of attempted first-degree murder and possession of firearm by a known felon, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:30, and 14:95.1. He was sentenced under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 as a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted first-degree murder and possession of firearm by a known felon. He was sentenced as a habitual offender to 45 years for the crime of attempted first-degree murder, to run concurrently with a 15-year sentence for the offense of felon in possession of a firearm. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient to support his attempted murder conviction. The jury was free to make a credibility determination and accept or reject witness testimony. Physical evidence, including casings found under the street lamp where defendant was seen shooting his gun, further substantiated eyewitness testimony. The State additionally proved that defendant had the requisite specific intent under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27 and 14:30 because the discharge of a firearm in the direction of a crowd of innocent bystanders was repeatedly been recognized as sufficient to prove specific intent to kill or inflict great bodily harm. His sentence was appropriate given the seriousness of his conduct, coupled with his proclivity for violence with firearms.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

969 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Rhone v. Ward


NO. 45,008-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,008 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/03/10); 31 So. 3d 591; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 126



February 3, 2010, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Rhone v. Ward, 34 So. 3d 291, 2010 La. LEXIS 1170 (La., Apr. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35642. Honorable Jenifer W. Clason, Judge.
Rhone v. Ward, 926 So. 2d 774, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 830 (La.App. 2 Cir., Apr. 12, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner brought an action against defendant prison officials in the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. The prisoner did not pay the filing fee as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186(A)(2). The prisoner failed to pay fees and costs for more than three years, and the case was dismissed pursuant to § 15:1186(B)(2)(c). The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186(B)(2)(c), a provision of the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA), a civil action filed by a prisoner could be dismissed if the prisoner failed to pay the court costs or fees within three years from the date the costs or fees were incurred. The prisoner argued that § 15:1186(B)(2)(c) violated the equal protection clause of the Louisiana Constitution and deprived him of his right to access of the courts under La. Const. art. I, § 22. The court held that neither indigents nor prisoners were suspect classes for equal protection purposes. Section 15:1186(B)(2)(c) clearly did not affect any fundamental right. Additionally, it was not discriminatory on the basis of any classification set forth in the equal protection clause of the Louisiana Constitution. Therefore, the statute merely had to be supported by a rational basis reasonably related to a legitimate governmental interest. The government had an interest in causing prisoners to weigh the decision to file lawsuits and in controlling its dockets. The provision was limited because it did not require the dismissal of all suits filed by prisoners, and thus, did not bar their access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court dismissing the prisoner's lawsuit without prejudice.

 

970 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Conner


NO. 2009-KA-1023


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-1023 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/03/10); 30 So. 3d 1132; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 156



February 3, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 8, 2010


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 445-972, SECTION "J". Honorable Darryl A. Derbigny, Judge.
State v. Conner, 996 So. 2d 564, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1308 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of attempted burglary, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:62. The maximum sentence was six years under § 14:27(D)(3). The district attorney alleged and proved that defendant was a quadruple offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Defendant was then sentenced to 20 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the proof that defendant was a quadruple offender, the trial court had sentenced defendant to one year. The court held that defendant's 20-year sentence was presumptively constitutional. Defendant bore the burden of clearly and convincingly establishing the excessiveness of his sentence by showing factually that the imposition of the sentence amounted to nothing more than the purposeful imposition of pain and suffering and was grossly out of proportion to the severity of the crime. No evidence was introduced in the district court in support of the claim of excessiveness of sentence, and the pre-sentence report was not included in the record on appeal. The court held that without the factual information in the pre-sentence report, it had no way of evaluating the reasonableness of the sentencing court imposing a sentence twenty times greater than the initial sentence. Defendant therefore failed to overcome the presumption that the sentence imposed upon him did not violate the proscriptions of the Eighth Amendment and of La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

State v. Otero


NO. 09-KA-468


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-468 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/26/10); 31 So. 3d 1125; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 108



January 26, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 31, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Otero, 45 So. 3d 1072, 2010 La. LEXIS 2154 (La., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-3095, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE LEE V. FAULKNER, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Otero, 3 So. 3d 34, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1697 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: MULTIPLE OFFENDER FINDING AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; MATTER REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. He challenged a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which found that he was a third felony offender and sentenced him to 66 years imprisonment without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by failing to find that the predicate convictions did not comply with the requirements of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 556.1. The court of appeal held that the predicate offenses were properly used to prove defendant's status as a multiple felony offender. In advising defendant of his constitutional right to confrontation codified in art. 556.1(A)(3), the trial court sufficiently apprised him of the encompassing rights under the Confrontation Clauses of the Sixth Amendment and La. Const. art. I, § 16 to physically face those who testified against him and to conduct a cross-examination of those adverse witnesses. The State met the burden of proving the existence of defendant's guilty pleas and that he was represented by counsel when the guilty pleas were taken. Defendant failed to show either that his rights were infringed or that there was a procedural irregularity in his guilty pleas. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive sentence. Defendant received the mandatory minimum sentence, and the State proved that he used force or intimidation while armed with a dangerous weapon, which were elements of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal affirmed defendant's multiple offender enhanced sentence. It remanded remand the matter for correction of the multiple offender commitment/minute entry to reflect that defendant was not informed of his Boykin rights.
