State v. Juengain


NO. 2009-KA-0425


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-0425 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/20/10); 41 So. 3d 499; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 65



January 20, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 25, 2010.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Juengain v. State, 83 So. 3d 1033, 2012 La. LEXIS 511 (La., Mar. 2, 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Juengain v. State, 176 So. 3d 1036, 2015 La. LEXIS 1865 (La., Sept. 11, 2015)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Juengain v. Louisiana, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 151273 (E.D. La., Sept. 14, 2016)
Related proceeding at Juengain v. Tervalon, 2017 La. App. LEXIS 1384 (La.App. 4 Cir., July 26, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 479-222, SECTION "F". Honorable Dennis J. Waldron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED CONDITIONALLY; MOTION TO REMAND GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of possession of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C)(2), and sentencing him to life imprisonment as a fourth offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Defendant also sought a remand to the trial court for consideration of his motion for a new trial pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 853.


OVERVIEW: First, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's suppression motion because it was reasonable for the arresting officers to suspect that a drug transaction had occurred and to initiate an investigatory stop. Next, defendant was properly tried before a six person jury because the punishment for a conviction for possession of cocaine was not necessarily confinement at hard labor. Defendant's status as a habitual offender had no bearing on the size of the jury because the habitual offender proceeding was a separate proceeding applicable only after conviction and then at the discretion of the district attorney. Although the instant offense involved possession of only a single piece of crack cocaine, defendant failed to meet the burden of proving that a life sentence was unconstitutionally excessive because he had been convicted previously of eight felonies and three misdemeanors, including the crimes of violence of sexual battery and molestation of a juvenile. However, defendant's motion for a new trial was timely filed under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 853 and, therefore, he was entitled to remand for consideration of the motion.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter to the trial court for consideration of defendant's timely-filed motion for a new trial.

State v. Allen


NO. 2009-KA-0813


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-0813 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/13/10); 30 So. 3d 1024; 2010 La. App. LEXIS 41



January 13, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 19, 2010
Writ denied by State ex rel. Allen v. State, 61 So. 3d 658, 2011 La. LEXIS 729 (La., 2011)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Allen v. State, 95 So. 3d 1068, 2012 La. LEXIS 2146 (La., 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Allen v. Prince, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60641 (E.D. La., Apr. 12, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 474-262, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of simple possession of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C), adjudicating him as a quadruple felony offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1A(1)(c)(i), and sentencing him to 20 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant's motion for reconsideration was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defense counsel failed to comply with the statutory requirements for properly preserving a claim for excessiveness on appeal under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 881.1, 881.2. However, the issue of excessiveness was procedurally preserved for review because defendant objected to the sentence upon denial of his motion to reconsider. Regardless, there were no facts in the record that individualized or particularized defendant or his circumstances. Thus, there was nothing substantive for the court to consider in determining whether the sentence was excessive. There was a discrepancy between the sentencing transcript and the minute entry in that the sentencing transcript failed to note that the sentence was to be served without benefit of parole as required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(A)(1). However, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:301.1(A) self-activated the correction and eliminated the need for remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Wilson


NO. 09-KA-108 Consolidated With NO. 09-KA-210


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-108 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/29/09); 30 So. 3d 149; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2219



December 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 31, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-3654, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE JOAN S. BENGE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession of marijuana with the intent to distribute, distribution of cocaine, and possession with the intent to distribute cocaine. He was sentenced as a multiple offender and received an enhanced sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his three drug convictions, his original sentence, and the adjudication on a multiple offender bill and enhanced sentence. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the denial of his motion for a continuance was appropriate. Defendant alleged that his trial counsel was ineffective. However, the instances in question occurred during trial, not prior to his request for a continuance to allow private counsel to prepare for trial. Defendant also had approximately two years between his arraignment and the date set for trial to retain the attorney of his choice, if he could manage to do so. There was no constitutional right to make a new choice of counsel on the date the trial was to begin, with the attendant necessity of a continuance and its disrupting implications to the orderly trial of cases. Further, in regard to his sentences, given the facts of the case and the fact that his enhanced sentence of 20 years was on the low end of the possible sentencing range, there was no error. Defendant committed three drug-related offense on the same day, sold drugs to an undercover officer, and had additional cocaine and marijuana found in his possession.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Oliver

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Oliver v. Rogers, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 37808 (E.D. La., Mar. 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-955, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Oliver, 857 So. 2d 1227, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2654 (La.App. 5 Cir., Sept. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; APPLICATIONS FOR WRITS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), entered judgment convicting defendant of theft of goods, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67.10, and sentencing her as a habitual offender to 20 years imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. After her conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal, defendant filed pro se writ applications, which were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: First, defendant claimed error in the admission of certain testimony regarding a juicer. However, even defense counsel referred to the juicer and, thus, defendant waived the issue. Regardless, the jury did not hear testimony about the seizure of a juicer. Next, defendant argued that § 14:67.10 was unconstitutional because it established different grades of penalties for the theft of goods from merchants than the general theft statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67, did for theft from other businesses and private persons. However, defendant did not raise the constitutionality issue in the trial court, so the issue was not preserved for review. Nonetheless, the appellate court noted that the argument also failed on the merits. Finally, defendant was not entitled to retroactive application of an amendment to the statute. Under the current version, defendant's crime would have been classified as a misdemeanor. However, the applicable sentencing scheme was the one in effect at the time the offense was committed. Defendant pointed to nothing in the enacting legislation or in the amended statute that indicated the new sentencing provisions should have been applied to her retrospectively.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ applications and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Evans


NO. 09-KA-477


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-477 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/29/09); 30 So. 3d 958; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2226



December 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 31, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Evans, 61 So. 3d 653, 2011 La. LEXIS 711 (La., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-1569, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Evans, 844 So. 2d 111, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 646 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 11, 2003)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR CORRECTION OF PATENT ERRORS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which sentenced him as a second felony offender to 45 yeas imprisonment at hard labor, with the first five years to be served without benefits, upon his conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A).


OVERVIEW: Originally, defendant was sentenced to 30 years without benefits. His original sentence was vacated and he was resentenced to 45 years without benefits as a habitual offender. On first appeal, defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the matter was remanded for rulings on defendant's two motions to reconsider sentence. On remand, the trial court denied both motions, but resentenced defendant by adding benefits after five years. Defendant did not file a motion to reconsider the resentence and, thus, appellate review of the enhanced sentence was limited to a review for constitutional excessiveness. The mid-range sentence was supported by comparison to similar cases and did not shock the sense of justice. Defendant had committed armed robberies as a juvenile and had a prior conviction for possession of cocaine. The trial judge imposed an illegally lenient enhanced resentence when he restricted benefits for only five years, but no corrective action was required because under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:301.1, the statutory requirement of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(G) that a habitual offender be sentenced without benefits was self-activating.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence, but remanded the matter for correction of patent errors.

State v. Beaudion


09-440


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-440 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/23/09); 27 So. 3d 342; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2195



December 23, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE TENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF NATCHITOCHES, NO. C-12786. HONORABLE DEE A. HAWTHORNE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches (Louisiana), convicting him on a jury's verdict of possessing a schedule II controlled dangerous substance, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, and sentencing him to serve five years at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went into a known crack house for the purpose of purchasing crack cocaine. When defendant left, he had crack cocaine in his pants pocket. When an officer asked defendant what he had in his pocket, defendant attempted to discard the drugs. Thus, defendant claimed that he lacked intent to possess. However, defendant went to the house with the intent to obtain crack cocaine. Further, defendant's attempt to conceal, then discard, the illicit substance shows that he was aware of the nature of the substance. Next, there was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for mistrial. The trial court did not err in reminding the jurors that six votes for guilty were required to return a guilty verdict because the jury indicated it had a verdict although subsequent polling revealed it was an invalid verdict. The grand jury foreperson did not state the jury had been unable to reach a verdict. Next, defendant's sentence was not excessive because he had an extensive criminal history, and had been regularly engaging in the illegal possession of crack cocaine. Finally, defendant's ineffective assistance arguments were relegated to post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Langlinais


09-422


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-422 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/16/09); 27 So. 3d 1011; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2136



December 16, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Langlinais, 2011 La. LEXIS 75 (La., Jan. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 07-2426. HONORABLE LORI ANN LANDRY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana) imposing concurrent sentences for convictions of possession with intent to distribute dihydrocodeinone, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:968(A)(1), and possession with intent to distribute cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to five years for the dhydrocodeinone charge and 10 years, with five years suspended, for the cocaine charge. It also ordered five years of supervised probation upon defendant's release, along with 12 special conditions of probation, including payment of fines and fees. Defendant was a first time offender, she was in poor health, and she was over 50 years of age. For possession with intent to distribute dihydrocodeinone, defendant received one-half of the maximum possible sentence and her fine was significantly less than the maximum possible fine. For possession with intent to distribute cocaine, the 10-year sentence was one-third of the maximum possible sentence, and defendant's fine was a fraction of the maximum possible fine. While the predicate sentences were reasonable, the special conditions of probation were exceptionally onerous for a disabled woman on an extremely limited income. Not only was defendant's financial situation unlikely to improve during her imprisonment or while serving probation, her medical diagnoses were chronic and would not likely improve as she aged.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence for possession with intent to distribute dihydrocodeinone was affirmed. Defendant's sentence for possession with intent to distribute cocaine was affirmed and amended by deleting the special conditions of probation, with the exception of reporting to the probation office within 24-hours of release, reporting monthly, and paying a monthly supervision fee.

State v. Wiltz


NO. 2008-KA-1441


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1441 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/16/09); 28 So. 3d 554; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2145



December 16, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 18, 2010.
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Wiltz, 2010 La. LEXIS 2699 (La., Nov. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 457-713, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana) entered judgment on a jury's verdict convicting defendant of aggravated assault on a peace officer with a firearm, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:37.2. The trial court sentenced defendant to 10 years, with credit for time served. Defendant's motion to reconsider the sentence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not denied a fair trial by the admission of testimony relating to the ownership of a car because the ultimate issue was one of whether the fleeing defendant pointed a loaded handgun at a police officer. Given defendant's testimony and inconsistent statements, the prosecutor's remarks during closing argument were neither unreasonable nor unduly prejudicial. Even if a challenged statement had not been made, the verdict would have been the same because any reasonable jury could have concluded that the evidence and testimony supported the State's case. Defendant's reason for fleeing the scene with the gun had no bearing on his decision to twice point the gun at the police officer. Furthermore, defendant was not denied his right to present a defense because he told the jury he could not leave the gun in the car. Defendant's assertion that the statement was not hearsay or an exception to the hearsay rule was immaterial. The trial court imposed the maximum sentence, and a review of the record showed an adequate factual basis for the sentence because, inter alia, the State had dismissed two additional charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Linnear


No. 44,830-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,830 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/09/09); 26 So. 3d 303; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2056



December 9, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 263, 258. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of second-degree battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1 and sentenced him to four years and nine months at hard labor, with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for the crime of second-degree battery. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and that the sentence was not excessive. Defendant argued that he struck the victim in self-defense, but it was clear that defendant's actions were neither reasonable nor necessary. Although the victim might have bumped into defendant and even flashed gang signs in his face, the response of beating the victim unconscious was unreasonable. The force was also unnecessary because defendant admitted that after the first punch, the victim was not in a position to fight back. Furthermore, the injuries sustained by the victim supported a conclusion that defendant had the specific intent to cause serious bodily injury under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:10(1). In regard to his sentence, in light of defendant's criminal history of violence to persons and the seriousness of the injuries suffered by the victim, the near maximum sentence was appropriately tailored to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Collins


NO. 09-KA-283


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-283 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/08/09); 30 So. 3d 72; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2052



December 8, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 31, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Collins, 2010 La. LEXIS 1908 (La., Sept. 3, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-4265, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE AMENDED, CASE REMANDED FOR CORRECTION OF COMMITMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession with intent to distribute heroin, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A), and sentenced him to imprisonment at hard labor for 35 years, the first five years without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The trial court denied defendant's motion to reconsider the sentence.


OVERVIEW: The State produced sufficient evidence to show that defendant constructively possessed the drugs. Officers watched defendant leave and enter a hotel room several times and four packages of heroin were later found in the room in plain view. The State also provided sufficient evidence to show that defendant intended to distribute the drugs. An officer witnessed defendant distributing drugs before the arrest, the heroin was packaged for distribution purposes, paraphernalia was found with it, and the amount retrieved was inconsistent with personal use. The issue of whether the prosecution improperly commented on defendant's post-arrest silence was not properly preserved for appeal because defense counsel failed to object to the testimony. The application of the plain error doctrine was unwarranted. With regard to other crimes evidence, defendant opened the door to the testimony, the verdict was unattributable to any other crimes reference, and thus, any error was harmless. However, the trial court erred in sentencing defendant to five years without benefits because § 40:966(B)(1) did not require the sentence to be without benefits. The sentence as amended was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and remanded the case to amend and correct the commitment to conform with the sentencing transcript. In addition, the court amended the sentence to allow the possibility of parole. The trial court was ordered to correct and amend the commitment to reflect the availability of parole accordingly.

State v. London


NO. 09-KA-398


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-398 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/24/09); 28 So. 3d 1150; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1982



November 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-5336, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE JUNE B. DARENSBURG, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. London, 954 So. 2d 170, 2007 La. LEXIS 979 (La., Apr. 20, 2007)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to manslaughter under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana). He was sentenced to 20 years. The State filed a habitual offender bill of information alleging that defendant was a second felony offender. Defendant stipulated to these allegations and was sentenced to 20 years without the benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The habitual offender bill of information alleged that defendant had a prior conviction for aggravated assault. The court held, in its errors patent review, that the bill was defective because the State sought to enhance defendant's manslaughter sentence based on an aggravated battery conviction that was not obtained until after the commission of the manslaughter. The underlying offense of manslaughter was committed on March 12, 2001. He was not convicted until September 26, 2007. The habitual offender bill alleged defendant was convicted of the predicate offense on November 29, 2001. Thus, the predicate conviction occurred after the commission of the underlying offense but prior to the conviction for the underlying offense. Defendant could not be a multiple offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 based on the predicate offense alleged in the multiple bill. Therefore, he could not be adjudicated as a multiple offender. Defendant's stipulation to the multiple bill did not waive this legal defect.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's stipulation to the habitual offender bill and remanded the matter to the trial court, so defendant could be re-sentenced as a first offender.

Smart v. W. Jefferson Med. Ctr.


NO. 09-CA-366


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-366 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/24/09); 28 So. 3d 1119; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1979



November 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2010.
Writ denied by Smart v. W. Jefferson Med. Ctr., 27 So. 3d 857, 2010 La. LEXIS 390 (La., Feb. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 644-155, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE ROBERT M. MURPHY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heirs filed a medical malpractice action against defendant healthcare providers in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana). The providers filed peremptory exceptions of prescription on the basis of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. The trial court granted the exception of prescription and denied the heirs' motion to declare La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(A) unconstitutional. The heirs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed an original claim for malpractice on October 13, 2006. The Patient's Compensation Fund confirmed receipt of this request by letters dated November 1 and 13, 2007. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(A), filing fees in the amount of $ 100 per defendant were due within 45 days from these letters, but they were not remitted timely. Although the patient died within the 45-day period, there was no provision in the law which allowed a longer period within which to pay the fees under such circumstance. The heirs' claim was then filed January 11, 2008. The malpractice occurred and was known to the heirs no later than November 8, 2006. As the original claim was invalid and without effect for the failure to timely pay fees, the original claim did not suspend the running of prescription, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(A)(1)(e), and the heirs' claim had clearly prescribed. The court rejected the heirs' claim that the filing fees unconstitutionally delegated a judicial function to the executive branch in violation of La. Const. art. II, § 2, because the fees were not imposed to raise revenue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Johnson


NO. 09-KA-454


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-454 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/24/09); 28 So. 3d 1125; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1987



November 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Johnson, 38 So. 3d 355, 2010 La. LEXIS 1582 (La., June 25, 2010)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 108 So. 3d 83, 2013 La. LEXIS 281 (La., Feb. 8, 2013)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 178 So. 3d 142, 2015 La. LEXIS 2048 (La., Sept. 18, 2015)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 215 So. 3d 677, 2017 La. LEXIS 782 (La., Apr. 13, 2017)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Johnson v. McCain, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 121615 (E.D. La., June 26, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 08-1774, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE JOHN J. MOLAISON, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED, REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two count of possession with intent to distribute cocaine and one count of possession of cocaine, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A),(C), and second offense possession of marijuana, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(C). The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), sentenced defendant to concurrent prison terms. It later granted defendant an out-of-time appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defense counsel filed a motion to withdraw and an accompanying Anders brief. On appeal, defendant challenged trial counsel's effectiveness. While trial counsel did not call any of his own witnesses at the suppression hearing, he cross-examined the State witnesses and questioned them about the confidential informants, the controlled buys, and the applications for the search warrants. Through his cross-examination, he effectively tried to discredit the State's evidence. Therefore, trial counsel offered effective assistance. Further, under the totality of the circumstances, the search warrants were issued based on probable cause. Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying the motion to suppress. Defendant's claim that the search warrants were invalid because they were unconstitutionally signed by a commissioner as opposed to a judge was a meritless argument because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:716(B)(1) was previously determined to be constitutional. However, the trial court erred in imposing the sentence on one count of possession with intent to distribute because under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B)(4)(b) only the first two years of a sentence should have been without benefits.


OUTCOME: The court amended defendant's sentence on count two to reflect only the first two years of the sentence was to be served without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence, as amended, and remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to amend the minute entry to reflect the amended sentence. It granted appellate counsel's motion to withdraw.

Rapides Parish Police Jury v. Catahoula Duck Club & Lodge L.L.C.


09-64


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-64 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/18/09); 24 So. 3d 988; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1971



November 18, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Rapides Parish Police Jury v. Catahoula Duck Club & Lodge L.L.C., 28 So. 3d 279, 2010 La. LEXIS 466 (La., 2010)
Related proceeding at Rapides Parish Police Jury v. Reich, 2011 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 224 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 231,119. HONORABLE DONALD T. JOHNSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police jury brought suit against defendant property owners in the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), seeking to nullify a public sale and to have a servitude across the property recognized. An owner filed exceptions of prescription and no cause of action. The trial court granted the exception of prescription, and the police jury appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the property was in administration due to its prior owner's death, the police jury sought to record a servitude agreement entitling it to a servitude on a gravel road across the property. The property was subsequently foreclosed on, and the property owners obtained their interest from the buyer at the foreclosure sale. The police jury received no notice of the foreclosure sale. The police jury argued that the servitude agreement conveyed to it a property interest entitling it to notice of the foreclosure proceedings, and that the failure to provide it with notice violated its due process rights as provided for in U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that the police jury was asserting that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3886.1, which provided a one-year prescriptive period for claims arising out of a failure to give notice of a sheriff's sale, was an unconstitutional limitation on due process. This claim could not be raised for failure to raise it in the trial court and comply with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:257(C) and La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1880. Because the sheriff's sale occurred in September 2006 and suit was not filed until April 2008, the action was prescribed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Davis


No. 44,656-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,656 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/18/09); 26 So. 3d 802; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1957



November 18, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Davis, 38 So. 3d 355, 2010 La. LEXIS 1572 (La., June 25, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davis v. Louisiana, 562 U.S. 1147, 131 S. Ct. 922, 178 L. Ed. 2d 769, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 113 (Jan. 10, 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Davis v. Cain, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 160974 (W.D. La., Aug. 8, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 262,971. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.
State v. Davis, 995 So. 2d 1211, 2008 La. LEXIS 2769 (La., Dec. 12, 2008)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND AGGRAVATED RAPE SENTENCE AFFIRMED; ORIGINAL INDECENT BEHAVIOR WITH JUVENILES SENTENCE REINSTATED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) entered judgment convicting defendant of aggravated rape, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42(A)(4), and indecent behavior, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81. Defendant was sentenced to death for the aggravated rape and a concurrent 7-year sentence for indecent behavior. On remand for resentencing, defendant was given life and a consecutive 7-year hard labor sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not err in admitting various other crimes evidence. Facts regarding defendant's previous sexually assaultive behavior were relevant to show other sexually assaultive behavior, as well as a lustful disposition toward young children. Evidence of defendant's guilty plea to second degree battery was admissible as an exception to the hearsay evidence rule under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803(22). Likewise, a certified copy of the bill of information charging defendant with the oral sexual battery was properly introduced into evidence as an exception to the hearsay rule under art. 803(8)(a)(iii). Testimony regarding a child's initial complaint of sexually assaultive behavior was admissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 804(B)(5). However, the trial court had no authority to amend the sentence for the indecent behavior. In his initial appeal, defendant sought review only of the constitutionality of the death penalty for aggravated rape. Thus, the trial court's change of the sentence for indecent behavior with juveniles, making it consecutive to the sentence of the other conviction, was outside the parameters of the remand order and the jurisdiction of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and the aggravated rape sentence. It reinstated the original concurrent indecent behavior with juveniles sentence and affirmed.

 

987 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Regis


NO. 2009-KA-0806


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-0806 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/12/09); 25 So. 3d 183; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1941



November 12, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 27, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Regis, 2010 La. LEXIS 1506 (La., June 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 473-670, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Q. Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED, AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of attempted possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1), and sentenced him to serve eight years at hard labor, without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence for the first two years.


OVERVIEW: The defense was not entitled to compel disclosure of the confidential informant because the informant was not a participant in the crime. Merely alleging that contradictory testimony was possible did not constitute exceptional circumstances or a concrete reason to disclose the informant's identity. Additionally, there was no indication that defendant's rights were prejudiced by non-disclosure. With regard to defendant's constitutional challenge to a jury instruction informing the jury that it did not have to reach a unanimous verdict, no contemporary objection was made to the instruction; thus, defendant arguably waived review of the claim. Further, there was no indication that the jury's verdict was less than unanimous. Finally, the appellate courts that have addressed the issue have rejected it. Defendant sentence had to be amended, however. Defendant was convicted of the lesser included offense of attempted possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. Accordingly, the trial court should have strictly construed La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:979(A) and given no minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, amended his sentence to delete the prohibition denying him benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence for the first two years, and affirmed the amended sentence.

State v. Ceaser


09-236


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-236 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/04/09); 21 So. 3d 1122; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1863



November 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Ceaser, 2010 La. LEXIS 1458 (La., June 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 75,429-FB. HONORABLE THOMAS F. FUSELIER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which convicted and sentenced him for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, possession of ecstasy with intent to distribute, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966, and of being a convicted felon in possession of a firearm, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1.


OVERVIEW: When officers responded to a report of suspected drug activity between two vehicles, defendant pulled his car away, parked in a nearby driveway, and declined permission to search the car. One officer was approached by a person, who requested the officers to remove the vehicle, which was parked on his mother's property. Defendant had left the car, entered this residence, and then left the scene. An inventory search prior to the car being towed disclosed a large amount of crack, a large bag of pills, a loaded pistol, and drug paraphernalia. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions. In particular, the record showed that defendant possessed the car, and thus, constructively possessed its contents. Officers testified that the amount drugs found in the car was not typical of individual use, and that the drug paraphernalia similarly indicated that the drugs were for distribution. The record also showed that defendant had prior felony drug convictions. The court found that the sentences were not unconstitutionally excessive because they were within the statutory ranges, and the trial court properly considered the applicable sentencing factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

989 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Insley


09-393


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-393 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/04/09); 22 So. 3d 258; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1874



November 4, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERNON, NO. 73136. HONORABLE VERNON BRUCE CLARK, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to attempted contribution to the delinquency of a juvenile, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:92(A)(11)(a). The Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon (Louisiana) sentenced him to three years at hard labor. Defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence was denied. Defendant appealed, challenging the excessiveness of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant knowingly smoked crack cocaine with a juvenile 12 years of age. Defendant argued that the maximum sentence for attempted contribution to the delinquency of a juvenile under § 14:92(A)(11)(a) was two and one-half years when the crime involved the possession of cocaine and that the three year sentence was excessive because he had medical problems and was wheelchair bound. Pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1(E), his second claim was not properly before the appellate court since he did not raise it in his motion for reconsideration. The underlying offense was possession of cocaine, which, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C)(2), carried a penalty of imprisonment with or without hard labor for not more than five years. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27(D)(3), the sentencing statute for attempt, imprisonment could not exceed one-half of the longest term of imprisonment prescribed for the offense so attempted. Therefore, defendant's penalty for attempted contribution to the delinquency of a juvenile by knowingly smoking crack cocaine was zero to two and one-half years.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was vacated and the case remanded to the trial court for imposition of a sentence that did not exceed two and one-half years.

 

990 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. A.D.A.


No. 44,791-JWC


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,791 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/28/09); 26 So. 3d 154; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1793



October 28, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Application for Writs from the First Judicial District Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 136265. Honorable E. Paul Young, III, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile was charged with first degree murder. The First Judicial District Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) denied applicant State's motion to transfer the case to the district court for prosecution of the juvenile as an adult pursuant to La. Child. Code Ann. art. 857. The State filed an application for supervisory writ.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile argued with his aunt's husband, the victim. The juvenile left the premises, but while the victim was calling 911, he returned, kicked in the door, entered the home, and shot the victim in the chest. At the time of the shooting, the juvenile was four days from his 15th birthday. The juvenile court erred in weighing the factors of La. Child. Code Ann. art. 862 because the State presented sufficient evidence to prove by clear and convincing evidence that there was no substantial opportunity for the juvenile's rehabilitation. The juvenile possessed the age and mental sophistication to understand his actions and their consequences. He had been processed through the juvenile justice system many times. Thus, he had the requisite mental sophistication to understand the charges against him. He had been diagnosed with mild mental retardation, ADHD, cannabis abuse, childhood onset conduct disorder, solitary aggressive type, impulse control disorder, bipolar disorder, personality disorder, and antisocial passive-aggressive compulsive features. However, no mental deficiencies were sufficiently profound to prevent the juvenile's knowledge and understanding of the charges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the juvenile court and remanded the matter for transfer to district court.

State v. Marshall


No. 44,759-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,759 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/28/09); 26 So. 3d 168; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1783



October 28, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Madison, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 111,501. Honorable Michael E. Lancaster, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of molestation of a juvenile, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2. He was adjudicated a second felony offender, and the Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Madison (Louisiana) sentenced to 30 years imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of diminution of sentence. He appealed, arguing that his 30-year sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the maximum sentence imposed was unconstitutionally excessive in that the trial court failed to consider his history and background, or the mitigating factors present in the case and that the goals of punishment and rehabilitation could be accomplished with a less harsh sentence. It did not appear that defendant filed a motion to reconsider sentence with the trial court; thus, review of his sentence was limited to a constitutional review of excessiveness. The trial court took cognizance of the criteria set forth in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. The court noted that defendant had an extensive criminal record dating back more than 20 years. Defendant also argues that his sentence, made pursuant to his status as a habitual offender, in effect, amounted to an unconstitutional, ex post facto application of the current stricter penalty for molestation of a juvenile. Because defendant was adjudicated a second felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(2)(a), the habitual offender sentencing range for molestation of a juvenile was not less than 7 1/2 years, nor more than 30 years with or without hard labor.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Delta Retail 45, L.L.C. v. Cox


No. 44,873-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,873 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/28/09); 26 So. 3d 200; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1828



October 28, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Delta Retail 45, L.L.C. v. Cox, 2010 La. LEXIS 283 (La., Feb. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Madison, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 09-09. Honorable Michael E. Lancaster, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Madison (Louisiana) granted summary judgment in favor of defendant law enforcement officials, dismissing plaintiff retail store's petition seeking the return of certain property seized during a criminal investigation. The retail store appealed.


OVERVIEW: The retail store sold adult magazines and movies. The law enforcement officials conducted a search and seizure of the store, seizing more than 9,000 items under a general search warrant. As a result, several individuals were charged with obscenity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106, but the retail store was not charged and was not a defendant in any related criminal proceeding. The retail store first filed suit in federal court under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988, seeking a temporary restraining order and a preliminary injunction ordering the return of the seized property. The federal court dismissed the suit on abstention grounds. The appellate court held that the trial court was correct in its determination that a civil proceeding was not the proper avenue for the retail store's attempt to gain the return of seized property being utilized as evidence in a criminal proceeding. The appropriate exclusive remedy in such case was a motion under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:41 in the criminal proceeding. The retailed store was entitled to file such pleading even though it was not a party to the criminal proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment dismissing the petition and ordered the retail store to pay costs.

State v. Anderson


NO. 09-KA-105


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-105 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/27/09); 28 So. 3d 324; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1820



October 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2010.
Writ denied by State v. Anderson, 2010 La. LEXIS 1239 (La., May 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-523, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE MARY H. BECNEL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND AS AMENDED AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fortieth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana), which convicted him of armed robbery with a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:64 and 14:64.3 and sentenced him to imprisonment at hard labor for 25 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his armed robbery conviction and sentence. The appellate court affirmed the conviction, amended the sentence to delete the illegal portion, and, as amended, affirmed the sentence. There was no indication that a juror had any problems listening to the evidence given his feelings about armed robbery. Thus, there was no need to rehabilitate him. The trial judge was present throughout the voir dire and could assess that juror's silent responses to the group questions. By failing to assert, when questioned, that he had a problem being a fair and impartial juror for any reason, he obviously convinced the trial judge that he was rehabilitated in the event his feelings somehow suggested bias against defendant. In regard to a second juror, by failing to assert his acquaintance or relationship with the parties mentioned, including the prosecutor, was such that he could not be fair and impartial in, and put aside, his personal acquaintance, that juror obviously convinced the trial judge that he was not biased. Given the trial judge's broad discretion in the matter, the appellate court was unable to say that it was erroneous to have denied the challenges for cause.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction but amended the sentence to delete the order of hard labor for the five-year enhancement under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.3. In all other respects, the sentence was affirmed.

 

994 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Marino v. Parish of St. Charles


NO. 09-CA-197


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-197 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/27/09); 27 So. 3d 926; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1817



October 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 60,668, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE BRADY M. FITZSIMMONS, JUDGE, AD HOC PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, sued appellee parish and alleged that as a result of the parish's negligence in maintaining its drainage system, homes and property were damaged/destroyed by flooding. The parish moved for summary judgment on the ground of immunity under, inter alia, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1. The Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles, Louisiana granted judgment for the parish. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner alleged that the parish was negligent in its operation of the drainage system, that the parish had a duty to keep the culverts clean and clear, to maintain them, and to operate the pumps in an effective and proper manner. The appellate court found that the decisions made in the instant case involved elements of judgment and choice, which meant that the parish's actions were discretionary under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1. The parish had shown the necessary social and economic consideration surrounding its decisions regarding the choice and operation of the drainage system for that specific area, including the fact that its system met the necessary standards. Further, there was nothing in the record to dispute the finding that the excess runoff caused by the intense rain caused the flooding, rather than any action taken by the parish. The longstanding jurisprudential rule of law in Louisiana was litigants had to raise constitutional attacks in the trial court, not the appellate courts, and the constitutional challenge had to be specially pleaded and the grounds for the claim particularized. None of the exceptions to that rule applied in the instant case.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of summary judgment for the parish was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the property owners.

Walker v. Appurao


NO. 2009 CA 0821


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 0821 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/23/09); 29 So. 3d 575; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2001



October 23, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Walker v. Appurao, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1962 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 18, 2009)
Writ denied by Walker v. Appurao, 28 So. 3d 1010, 2010 La. LEXIS 547 (La., Mar. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Washington, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 96544. Honorable Martin E. Coady, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed a judgment of the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Washington, Louisiana, granting an exception filed by defendants, physicians and their insurers, raising the objection of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and dismissing, with prejudice, the inmate's medical malpractice claims.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sued defendants over treatment he received at an outside state-operated medical facility. The district court dismissed the inmate's claims because he did not seek review of his medical malpractice claims either within the prison's administrative review process or before a state medical review panel as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39(E)(1). On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that under § 40:1299.39.1(A)(1)(a) prisoners were not required to submit their medical malpractice claims to a medical review panel prior to filing suit. The court held that § 40:1299.39.1 had to be read in pari materia with the provisions of § 40:1299.39(E)(1), which clearly stated that prisoners' medical malpractice claims arising under the Malpractice Liability for State Services Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 et seq., were to be submitted to be submitted to a medical review panel in accordance with § 40:1299.39.1. Because the inmate failed to exhaust his administrative remedies prior to filing suit in the district court, it lacked subject matter jurisdiction to consider his claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed insofar as it granted defendants' exception raising the objection of lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The judgment was amended to provide for dismissal of the inmate's claims without prejudice.

Hunter v. Jindal


No. 45,130-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


45,130 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/13/09); 20 So. 3d 592; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1747



October 13, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Hunter v. Jindal, 18 So. 3d 1292, 2009 La. LEXIS 3058 (La., Oct. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 09-3625. Honorable Wilson Rambo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; MOTION TO STRIKE DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor, individually and in his official capacity, sought review of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which found in favor of appellees, the governor, judge, secretary of state, and registrar of voters, and dismissed the mayor's petition challenging the certification of a recall petition and the scheduling of a recall election. The mayor also filed a motion to strike.


OVERVIEW: The mayor appealed from a judgment dismissing his petition challenging the certification of a recall petition and the scheduling of a recall election for his office; the appellate court affirmed. Election contests were to be decided quickly; likewise, the need for the finality of elections was of a very high priority. Given the strong public policy reasons underlying the short delays in election matters, the mayor failed to demonstrate that the notice or delay periods involved were violative of his due process or equal protection rights. Moreover, he failed to show any defect in the notice procedure, such as a defect in publication per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1300.7, that would have affected his ability to timely pursue the action. It was not a case in which the mayor showed no notice to the official publication. In fact, the evidence showed that the registrar and clerk of court received the document well within the 15-day period. There was no error in the findings regarding the relevant dates of the issuance of the proclamation and the filing of the lawsuit. Thus, the finding that the action was barred by peremption was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the mayor's motion to strike an attachment to the appellees' brief was denied. However, in deciding the case, the appellate court considered only those matters included in the record or those of which the appellate court was entitled to take judicial notice.

State v. Strother


09-110


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-110 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/07/09); 19 So. 3d 598; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1726



October 7, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted State v. Strother, 34 So. 3d 853, 2010 La. LEXIS 1163 (La., 2010)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Strother, 49 So. 3d 372, 2010 La. LEXIS 2264 (La., Oct. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 287123. HONORABLE THOMAS MARTIN YEAGER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE FOR ATTEMPTED SECOND DEGREE CRUELTY TO A JUVENILE REVERSED AND SET ASIDE. JUDGMENT OF ACQUITTAL ENTERED. CONVICTION FOR CRUELTY TO A JUVENILE AFFIRMED. SENTENCE VACATED. REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which convicted and sentenced him for attempted second-degree cruelty to a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27 and 14:93.2.3, and cruelty to a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:93.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his jury convictions and sentences for attempted second-degree cruelty to a juvenile and cruelty to a juvenile. The appellate court reversed and vacated the conviction and sentence for attempted second-degree cruelty to a juvenile. His conviction for cruelty to a juvenile was affirmed but that sentence was vacated due to excessiveness, and the case was remanded for resentencing. There was insufficient evidence regarding an act or acts by defendant that would have resulted in the injury to the baby's arm on February 2. Therefore, there was nothing to support a conviction for intentional or criminally negligent mistreatment or neglect of the child and there was no testimony indicating that defendant was alone with the baby when the injury to her arm occurred. Although defendant's conviction for cruelty to a juvenile was appropriate, the maximum sentence amounted to a needless and purposeless imposition of pain and suffering. The seriousness of the offense did not justify the maximum sentence since defendant was not one of the most blameworthy offenders; he was a first-time felony offender.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and vacated the defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted second-degree cruelty to a juvenile; affirmed his conviction for cruelty to a juvenile, but vacated that sentence; and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Suire


09-150


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


09-150 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/07/09); 19 So. 3d 640; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1703



October 7, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 13617-06. HONORABLE DAVID KENT SAVOIE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which convicted him of computer-aided solicitation of a minor, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.3, and sentenced him to three years at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made contact with an undercover agent posing as a 15-year-old girl in an internet chat room. The appellate court found sufficient evidence to convict defendant because his conduct fell within the scope of § 14.81.3. Defendant attempted to induce or entice a person whom he believed to be a 15-year-old girl into engaging in sexual conversation and masturbation. He discussed his past sexual history, the size of his penis, and the victim's experience with phone sex. These were all topics of a lewd or lascivious nature. The existence of the term "presence" in the statute did not limit its enforcement to only those acts committed in the actual physical presence or the immediate vicinity of the victim. It merely described the eventual hoped-for contact. The trial court did not abuse its discretion with regard to defendant's sentence, considering he intentionally communicated with a person whom he believed to be a 15-year-old girl, gained her confidence over several days, encouraged her to participate in sexual activity, and ultimately exposed himself via webcam while masturbating. Defendant's sentence was near the minimum possible sentence and he was spared a possible fine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Matthews


NO. 09-KA-180


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-180 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/29/08); 22 So. 3d 1098; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1663



September 29, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-1569, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) to one count of aggravated rape of a child, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. He filed an out-of-time appeal, seeking to withdraw his guilty plea, arguing that he had pled guilty in order to avoid the death penalty, a punishment that had since been found unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that his life sentence was excessive. He argued that the inducement for his guilty plea had been eliminated and that it would be fundamentally unfair to allow his plea to stand. The State responded that he was never exposed to the death penalty, pointing out that the indictment listed the offense as a class II felony and that the record was devoid of any evidence that defendant was induced to plead guilty due to threats of a death sentence. Defendant did not suggest that his guilty plea was constitutionally infirmed, and an inspection of the record did not reveal such a deficiency. At the time of his guilty plea, the district court advised him of the three Boykin rights, the district court further explained that the penalty for the charged offense was life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, and defendant indicated that he had discussed the matter with his attorney and that he understood the nature of the charge against him and the possible penalty. Pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2A(2), he was precluded from arguing that his sentence was excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1000 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ashley


No. 44,655-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,655 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/23/09); 22 So. 3d 1045; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1640



September 23, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Ashley, 34 So. 3d 271, 2010 La. LEXIS 1024 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at D.O.C. v. Cain, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 72862 (W.D. La., May 5, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 258,204. Honorable John Mosely, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, defendant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping, attempted forcible rape, first degree robbery, and aggravated flight from an officer and he was sentenced. Defendant appealed. Defense counsel filed two assignments of error pertaining to sufficiency of the evidence and excessive sentences. Defendant filed 17 pro se assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: There was ample evidence supporting the convictions. The victim was forcibly seized in a parking lot and forced with the use of an apparent weapon to get in her vehicle with defendant. Defendant took the victim from one place to another as he drove her around making various stops. On the question of whether he had the intent to take something of value, the examples were abundant. Defendant's conviction for first degree robbery, attempted forcible rape, and aggravated kidnapping did not violate his constitutional double jeopardy right. The state showed that defendant abducted the victim and took her from one place to another with the intent of forcing her to give up the use of her car, money, and sex in the hope of being set free. The fact that in some cases he resorted to additional crimes to actually get those things did not give rise to a double jeopardy claim. Because defendant's statements to the police had already been ruled as admissible in the pretrial hearing, the state was entitled to refer to them as a confession in the opening statement. Defendant's sentences were neither grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offenses nor shocking to the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.
